O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O ye, very dear children, I have finished this book which is the end of the science of medicine assembled from its employment, and I have completed it by its exposures and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And I saw in vision that I must complete this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely surgery.
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is fraught in our region and is strange to all, if the science is lost and forgotten, and nothing remains of it except for the little descriptions in the books of the ancients which the hands have performed.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this arises the error and the vanity, and the closures of the understanding and the displacement of the science.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	Or it seems to me that I must bring it to life together the ordination of this practitioner according to the way of exposure and declaration and abbreviation; and I will join together the forms of the instruments of cautery and other instruments of the work with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation of it, as it is necessary. And because no wise man of hands is found in our time, the art of medicine is prolonged.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And he must know who comes into this subject thoroughly the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so long as he can discern the judgments of the limbs, and the forms and the joints and the separations of them, and has knowledge of bones and nerves and veins and arteries and the number of seeds, and the movement of semen and its rest.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And thus Hippocrates taught us that with the hand we must not be lazy, but must work diligently; and the same in the art of healing.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We must say at the outset of this book that whoever is not learned in the things that are before him, if he is arrogant and does not humble himself; as I have often seen happen, many people ruin themselves through these very things that are related to this science and abandon both science and sense.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I have seen a madman who copped his testicles with a pincer, or pulled out the hair of a woman; and he bled so much that the woman died in his hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And thus another marvel which treats a stone of a bladder, and the stone was great; if it carried away with it a piece of the bladder, and remained in the hon for two days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have already heard of it being called to treat, and I saw the disposition of the patient and the greatness of the stone, and indeed if it were cut out it would surely die.</start_of_turn>
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And thus another marvel which treats a limb broken in our land, and with the bruise caused by the wound; and the physicians of this land do not know how to treat the bruise upon the wound as these stars are held together by strong ligature, and do not allow the wound to bleed at all, and leave it thus until it is finished; and they command that it not be moved, and that the limb be entirely freed and the bone and marrow be lost forever.</start_of_turn>
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I come to him and hasten to loosen the limb; and when I find it dislocated, it is without pain and without feeling any discomfort.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But in every way the corruption has already been confirmed or the limb has become deformed, and it cannot be healed; and the corruption continues to grow as long as the limb remains whole and intact.</start_of_turn>
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And thus too with other matters which undermine the body, such as tumors, boils, and inflammation caused by the malice of its master.</start_of_turn
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a wound caused by a melancholic tumor, it is only useful to touch it with fire if it is not in some part already corrupted to such an extent that everything corrupted must be removed.</start_of_turn
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And thus, take heed, for the work of the hands has become divided into twelve parts: that is to say, there is peril in many things. I will show in each chapter where there is doubt and peril.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	For you must always be wary, lest the fools speak evil of you
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	If you take your arms in custody, and undertake your diseases gently and firmly, and use the better way so that by the grace of God you come to health and be saved; and leave the contagious diseases in their natural state; and stay armed in this way so that you can go from this world to the next in peace.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»	Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»
J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc .iij. chapitres.	The physician rejoins the discourse, reminding the reader of the two preceding chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter deals with fire cautery and surgical cautery with water-based medicine, and this chapter orders from the head down; forms of instruments, and instruments for cautery, and everything necessary for the work
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter deals with fracture and piercing, and of abscesses and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and this chapter orders and the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter deals with restoring dislocations and strains, and similar matters; and it is ordered from the head downwards, and from the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	So, as we have recalled from the work, it is necessary to say what is the quality of the aid and the danger of neglecting complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of the aid, and the danger, is the longest word and the most subtle science and the secret response; and concerning this, many speak, and they agree with this; and I find that their words are insufficient, because I reduce the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that the fire cautery helps universally for all complexion or when there is matter, for since there are two complexions: that is to say a complexion that is warm in sense of matter, and a complexion that is dry in sense of matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For in complexion hot and dry mixed with matter, some say it brings no relief and declare that cautery is of great aid; others say the opposite: that cautery is of no value in disease except when it comes from heat and dryness.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of a man and his moisture with the complexion of the fire, you find the body dry.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree to this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have never found it to be otherwise by experience.</start_of_turn>
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And every way, there is no fire that does not yield to me more than that which has been proved by experience, and which knows by long experience the chapter of cauteries, and the variety of humoral conditions, and the causes and dispositions of their diseases, and the issues and the space of their tensions; of other humors we have no fear, even in cold and moist diseases.</start_of_turn
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the others yield to the cautery and agree with it.</start_of_turn
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know this, children, that fire cautery is more effective for certain ailments than burning medicines.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For the fire is simple, and brings no further pain than to the limb that is being treated, and harms no other part besides that.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	Burning medicines come from one limb to another, causing ailments in other parts and causing the patient to suffer more.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The fire, because of its height and for the goodness of its substance, does not cause much pain, if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	The fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	Know ye, son, that it is necessary to agree in what tense the cauteries should be made, and their precautions.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	I say that the cautery is permissible in all tenses, for the harmful effects that are coming from it are overcome by the aid of the cautery; and besides, if the cauteries are for necessary pains that are urgent and cannot wait for a greater harm to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And think not, my son, that because fools do, it follows that the malady which is cured by cautery has no remedy; for he says it is so. But he lies, for cautery is nothing but medicine which moves the complexion and dries humors which are the cause of pain, and is more useful than medicine for hastening its value and for the virtue of its work and its lordship.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And know that no disease ever departs according to the complexion of the patient and the course of the disease and its virtue; and are gathered in it the superfluities by the acquisition of meats and similar things, if these are not administered with cautery when there is little superfluity and moisture, for indeed cautery is better for pain than meats and similar things, and part of the pain does not return again; but this is often the case.</start_of_turn>
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand that because cautery is called behind medicine, and it is true; but they do not believe that cautery is better than medicine, but their understanding is false, for indeed cautery is behind medicine because whenever we administer other treatments for any disease and they do not help, then we administer the cautery, and it is better.</start_of_turn>
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, although cautery is behind medicine, it is not according to the intentions of fools.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients say that gold cautery is duller than iron, and they say that fire is only useful for the quality of the gold and for its fineness; and they say that the lead of the cautery does not cause harm, but this is not true, for I have proved it, and I have found that it is seen in some men; and gold cautery is worth as much as iron, as they say.</start_of_turn>
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And indeed, when you burn the instrument of gold, you do not know how much it is tarnished by the color of gold, and when it is so cold; and if you burn it too much; if there is too much fire; and thus there is enough hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we use our fire cautery, as we have learned it in our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or you have commanded this chapter from head to toe, for this reason that the way should be easier to find.</start_of_turn>
dou cautere olivaire	olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	These olive oil cauteries are useful for moisture and cold, for there are many diseases caused by a condition called "soda," and by the abundance of humors that descend from the head as sweat, and in the ears, and for many other complaints such as toothache, earache, and neck and throat pain, and even for many diseases that arise from cold, such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is such that the patient is purged by means of a soluble medicine which modifies the head of the joint, two or three times, according to what the physician deems useful and agreeable to the patient's custom; and then repeat the head of the joint of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	Then he makes him sit between your hands, and put his hands down on his feet; after that put the root of your thumb on the root of his thumb between his two nails; and there or will come your two middle fingers, if it bleeds from the base then withdraw the cautery which is called "olive", for this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put out the sign of ink, and make descending and extracting your hand back and forth; then withdraw your hand slightly, and renew the cautery until you see the bone somewhat; and if you do not see it, continue the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you; after that take one moment of balsam, and put in awe and soak a cotton pad inside, and take out the bone, and leave it for two days; after that put on a soft bandage. And leave it on until the scab has become bony; after that cure the wound of the burn which is called "tetrafarmaçon", until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And they say the ancients, that the more time passes over a wound, the more it purges; and for this reason they aid the wound with movement.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they say that none of these men say that we must leave the cautery on for so long that part of the bone is burnt, and then we must renew what is burnt on the bone, and it must be cured.</start_of_turn>
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And others say that we must leave the cautery on for so long as a woman puts in her girdle for that the humors issue out loosely; and we must leave the wound open for a long time; and then we must cure and dress it.</start_of_turn>
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two ways of cauterizing do not seem to me to be good for all things, for in some men or if there is fear of pain; and I think that I ought to leave it; for the head of the shoulder is easily loosened by the continuous solutions of nature, as we have seen in other members; and even when the pain is slight by nature, the first semblance of cautery is more salve and merciful for me, and for this reason I do this thing in this manner.</start_of_turn
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	From the ancient pain of the head.
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When there is chronic pain in the head that lasts a long time, the patient must use herbs, pills which are called «cochie», and vomiting of the head, oils and poultices; and if we make the cautery as we have said before, it is of no avail.</start_of_turn>
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care that if the patient’s condition is strong and not too weak; then the cautery must be performed as we have said above.</start_of_turn
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After the cautery is done on the bone of the head as we have said, and you have done the cautery of the vein which is called the «vasselz»; and that is where you put the sponges; hold your hand so that you do not see blood until the bone: the patient feels more great pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of that later; and it is recommended that the cautery of the horns be more subtle than that of the middle of the head, and that is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	Dou cautere dou chief,
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	Dou cautere dou chief,
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	When in a part of the shoulder comes sudden pain, and the disease is extended up to the armpit, and the limb is expelled by medicines that are modified, and other cures have been made as I said in the division of diseases; and all this has not profited: therefore you must make cauteries in two ways, that is to say of medicine and fire.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the cure of inflammation while he is still sane; and if you see that he does not recover from this with any of the medicines I have written or if you wish to treat him with other medicines that are not mentioned.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere. Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	The iron cautery is as it is written above. Make the cautery like this:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "closed" because its head is made in the shape of a loop or it has a slight curve, and in the middle there is a small appearance; and put out the painful limb, and hold your hand and touch the burn with a slight movement until half of the thickness of the hair is burned; and keep your hand still so that the artery does not burn, that is to say that it is blistered, and drain abundance of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After having put on cotton wool around the limb, take it out after two or three days. Then put on moist cotton wool in the burrow and cure the limb of swelling until it is healed. de emigraine	After having put on cotton wool around the limb, take it out after two or three days. Then put on moist cotton wool in the burrow and cure the limb of swelling until it is healed. Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you cauterize an abscess as we have previously said in the chapter on diseases, and it does not benefit, and you see that it does not suffice with just the cautery, then you must abstain from the cautery which is called "cultellare" while it is still green; and if you must remove the limb leaving a mark of half an inch long, and you move your hand once, and strain so that you do not cover the artery and do not feel pain; and be wary of the jaw that bites when you move it, and that it does not cause more damage than the pain and spasm, and be wary of the evacuation of blood from the artery when it is cut, or cutting causes great fear and discomfort to those who do not know how to handle it, and who are not experienced and learned; and leave the work in peace; but I will tell you how to staunch blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it is in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	If you notice that the former cautery does not suffice for the ailment, and the patient is suffering, cauterize the other side as well as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; and if you see that, administer the cautery that we have said or the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has a pair of scissors; and this cautery is better than the previous and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	If you notice that the former cautery does not suffice for the ailment, and the patient is suffering, cauterize the other side as well as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; and if you see that, administer the cautery that we have said or the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has a pair of scissors; and this cautery is better than the previous and more helpful.

Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture that must be cured by cautery is not fierce except for those that move from moisture, as we have said in the divisions of diseases; and do not make any cautery that resembles that which comes from drying and swelling of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this semblance of torture that is made of fumes of hydras and purges of head and gargling, know that it is worth nothing; therefore, you must cauterize the patient with two cautery irons. One in the root of the ear, the other at the temple, and the third at the junction of the two eyebrows. Place the cautery iron in the part that opens well and make it cauterize at the head of the ear below the tip of the earlobe, and another at the temple as long as one eye. And leave the cautery iron in place until half of the hair is burnt; this is the form of the cautery.
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it is the semblance of a cutlass that we have placed before you, but it is a more subtle and effective remedy than the knife; after treating like this, as I have said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is ancient and you cure it as we have said, and it does not profit, and the patient does not have fever, then you must make three cauteries: one on each corner of the head, one in the middle of the head, and one in the part called "vasselz" as we have said before, and the last cautery on the back of the stomach; and it is cured as we have said before
de litargie	De litargie.
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	When lying down. The patient must be given large doses of wine and cooling pills to soothe the brain; afterwards lie the head of the patient down and put on the crown of his head a patch of rue that is written or treat with poultices; and that is the manner of the fire cautery: as I have said.</start_of_turn>
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit. de la froidor dou chief	From the cold of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	From the cold of the head, it must be known that the head must be freed from hair and that which has been said previously; after which, when the patient’s head has been raised, then make the cautery between the nape of the neck and behind the ear, and in front of the collarbone; and if you must do more than this, and the limb is moist and the patient is fainting, and the sickness is violent, do three cauteries on the spine of the back; and let it remain as long as the hair is black, and keep your hand still; after which, cure as long as it is safe, and be the cautery which is called “olive” which has been said previously.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The fiery cautery must not be used except in cases of phlegmatique inflammation; and first of all modify the head of the year and other treatments that we have mentioned in the preceding chapter when the patient is large and suffering from excessive medical treatment.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a feeble patient who cannot bear suffering, make him garglement and chew, modifying the head of the year often with bones of flesh; afterwards raise the head up to the middle and make one cautery as we have said before, and one cautery on the vein and on the spleen; and if the patient is strong and suffering, make cauteries as we have said to those who have paralysis and softening of bones, on the spine of the back and neck, or the olive cautery as I have said.</start_of_turn>
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is feeble, make one subtle cautery as follows:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When melancholy is the cause, superflous or corrupted humors and large phlegm arise, then indeed we cauterize with certain cauteries as we have said to the paralytic.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	When melancholy is the cause, if the superflous humor descends to melancholy and the body of the patient is moist, then let him drink something to cause the brains to be relaxed, as is done before in the division.</start_of_turn>
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, take the patient’s chief; then make a circle of lint well made, like a circle, and put it on the chief; and hold the patient’s limbs crossed, and keep them well secured from all sides; then bring the flame and burn a little barley chaff; and keep the fire temperate so that the patient can tolerate it; then remove the circle from the chief and let it cool; do this for the patient once every week with another good government, until he is healed.</start_of_turn>
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere. Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	If you see the burn cauterized by making several pricks throughout the burn. This method of cautery soothes the brain instantly; then put on moist cotton wool in butter and lard.
de l’awe des eulz	If you see the burn cauterized by making several pricks throughout the burn. This method of cautery soothes the brain instantly; then put on moist cotton wool in butter and lard.
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the sign of the evacuation of blood first appears, as I have said in the division, then immediately order the patient to drink something that will solidify the head and keep it away from all moisture, and make him sweat or bathe more times when fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as .ij. eulz ensamble, ou en .i. se li dessendemens est en .i.; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After that you command him to rest his head, and you cauterize him around the head, and make three cauteries on each temple if the swelling of the blood has descended from the head as two together, or if it has descended from one side; and cut through all the veins and arteries that are below the eyebrow, and let the cautery be as long as the width of the temple; and take care not to remove too much blood, for if there is too much blood loss, if it is necessary, stop the bleeding with a piece of leather like you do.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les .ij. os derrier. dou cors des larmes	And I shall teach you concerning the extraction of arteries and the incision of the cautery how you shall extend it; and in no way shall you make the cautery or the lancet pierce the joints of the marrow bones behind
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere.
