dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	For the pain of tears through the eyes,
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide .iij. nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai .ij. cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les .ij. sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you have taken the medicine as we have said in the division, and it has not helped, then give the patient two fingers of wine; after that raise the head and make cautery or mix of olive oil; and make three cauteries of the cautery which is called "clavilis" on the two nipples, one at each breast; and be careful not to burn the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	This is the form of the cautery which is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare». de coi ci est li forme:	When the paper of the oil is softened by disease and moisture, then the cautery of this cautery which is called "olive" is done. Thus is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see that you must perform cautery upon the hairs of the armpits, let them grow as long as the hairs of the armpits themselves; and do not leave the hand but firm until the third part of the hair has been burned, as I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	And if you see that you must perform cautery upon the hairs of the armpits, let them grow as long as the hairs of the armpits themselves; and do not leave the hand but firm until the third part of the hair has been burned, as I have said.</start_of_turn>
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Never before have I seen that the hairs of oil have been converted to beards, and prick the oil, and it makes cautery in two ways: that is to say by fire, or by burning medicine.</start_of_turn
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they are born and even, then the physician should put the patient in a safe position; after that, mark on the skin of the eyes a figure which is as much like a flame as possible, or as the beginning of a sign from the hair; then he should put a moist cloth in butter and a little salve on the oil, and then cover the cautery with this form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing on the mark that you have made, and doing this several times, so that the burn is neither too deep nor too shallow; and the sign of the work is that you see the membrane withdraw, and the hair is raised to the point of the oil; then you should keep your hand still, and let them rest for two days; then put a moist cloth in butter until the swelling has gone down; after that, apply an ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after that the hairs grow, and the papere is softened, then restart the cautery on the same place as before; and if the hairs are plucked out, burn them as long as the papere returns to its natural state, and be even, and do not prick the hairs with the oil.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The burning cautery of medicine is that you command the patient to let the hairs grow large and even, then make parchment of the shape of a bay leaf; then take soap of France and live chalk, each a third, and grind them together well; and make it thick, so that it does not reharden, then put it on the shape that you have made like a bay leaf, and put the papere on the eyes; and if the disease persists in oil only, you must open in oil only, and if in both; and put cotton wool soaked in oil around the wound; and the head of the shoulder must be in its natural position and your thumb showing on the medicine, and press once and let it move every time the patient feels a biting of the medicine, for he feels biting just like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, if the medicine has reached your thumb.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien. Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bite is gone, if you lift the limb high, and you see the wound lift just as if it had been lifted by the contraction of fire or by incision; and if it is firm, it is well. If not, if you repeat the treatment on the limb or the treatment has not worked, until your works are even, and your wounds are at a point; then put on a moist bandage over the wound as long as the pain persists, and cure the limb of the swelling which is called "dyafenis" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.  Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if you have taken great care of your work and there is no longer any need for medicine, and if the wound becomes soft after that, and the hair is pricked with oil, if you repeat the treatment on that limb which has become softened by the wound, just as you did before; then cure until it is healed; and this is the form of the perfect cure.
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	Know that the souls of men are diverse in greatness and smallness, and according to that are your constraints; and do not be afraid to take another way to that which is studied by this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the treatment of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatment brings no benefit, then you must cauterize according to this manner
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to hold his head still; and hold his ears between your hands in such a manner that he does not move them, does not lower his head; then put a wet cloth or vinegar juice on the oil; then burn the cautery which is partly: and keep it over the head as if it were a goose feather; gather up what has been cauterized if you see it, if there is a point from the one ear to the other; and if you see that there is a burn similar to a burn; but whatever happens, that which is over the head is worth more than your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula until it is over, and draining the pus, and drying; and if it is closed, if the wound, and drain the wound; then put the cautery on hot and hold your hand over the cautery at the part of the thumb next to the oil, so that your hands do not tremble; and put the cautery in the grease of the oil, and hold it firmly.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien. Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse .iij. jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se .xl. jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If you approach the fire cautery at the beginning until the bone, that would be well. If this does not suffice, restart the cautery once more; otherwise, if you have done it carelessly, leave it for two days; then place a moist bandage on the burn and treat the desiccation until it heals, and if thirty days pass and it is still not healed, apply corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed; and then follow what is written in your chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent. Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure .i. camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	And there is a method of cautery for fistula which none of the ancients have mentioned. Understand fistula, and open the vessel; then put into the split .i. a little piece of gauze which is like this:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and I make to the quantity of a third of an ounce; and hold your hand or gauze firmly, and do not move the patient, only that the melted wax does not come into contact with it; and it is advisable to put on the patient's oil a moist bandage of wool or cotton: the wax will thus adhere to the vessel of the fistula, and the patient will recover with great marvel at the health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin. Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If the fistula is cured by the cautery as we have said, that is good. If not, if you must, administer a perforation to the nerve, and bring the fistula back to its normal place as it should be in its proper place.
des crevaices en levres	If the fistula is cured by the cautery as we have said, that is good. If not, if you must, administer a perforation to the nerve, and bring the fistula back to its normal place as it should be in its proper place.
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	If the fistula is cured by the cautery as we have said, that is good. If not, if you must, administer a perforation to the nerve, and bring the fistula back to its normal place as it should be in its proper place
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you have treated these cracks resulting from the divisions we mentioned, and the cure has not profited, then you should perform a small cautery culture according to this fashion:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you have treated these cracks resulting from the divisions we mentioned, and the cure has not profited, then you should immediately perform a small cautery culture in that area until the pain ceases; after the cure, keep the limb still until it has healed.</start_of_turn>
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the armpit.
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When the abscess comes to the root of the arm or the elbow, or the shoulder or the root of the teeth, after making the opening and the wound becomes swollen and forms a fistula; and you should cure it as we have mentioned in the divisions, and it will not profit: so it is necessary that you have a small cautery according to the quantity of the fistula; after you have cauterized the opening or perforation of the fistula, and keep your hand still until it has healed at the front and behind; and do this once or twice, after the cure of what we have mentioned in the cures, until it is healed; and if it is cured thus, that is good; but if not, you must uncover the limb and remove the corrupted bone, as you will find in this chapter.
dou movement des dens	The movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you have cured it with medicine, this is of no avail; therefore put the patient’s hand in your own; after that withdraw the cautery which will form afterwards in part as if you were putting on a pincer; and put the cautery into the tooth socket immediately, and hold your hand until the patient feels the heat coming from the root of the tooth; after that withdraw your hand and resume the cautery as you please; after that fill the patient’s mouth with salt water, and keep it closed for an hour and a quarter.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in part, when the teeth which were moving are confirmed, and the soft gum is restrained, and the moisture is corrupted, it dries up.
de la dolor des dens	De la douleur des dents.
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When toothache comes from cold, or there is cold or heat, and medical cures do not help, then it is necessary to perform cautery in two ways: cautery of the nerve and cautery of the fire.</start_of_turn>
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cautery of the burn if such be that you grasp a burn of grease, and the end in a spoon of iron or pewter; after taking cotton and wrapping over the tip of a rag, and the boil in grease boils, and put upon the aching tooth immediately and hold until it is cold; and do this often until the remedy comes to the root of the tooth, and if you see if there is still grease and cotton in the grease, and put upon the aching tooth, and put on the iron again until the fire comes to the cheek of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain. Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	The cautery of fire if such be that you grasp a cauldron of iron or pewter, and either large if the fire does not come to the mouth of the patient; after heating the cautery, as it will be shaped afterwards, and put it upon the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cold; do this often, for the pain will be as great from the inside as from the outside. And it is expedient that the patient fill his mouth with good grease in the process of this cautery, and then take it out; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make the cautery as you please, and according to what you have seen fit; and this is the form of the burn.
des scrophules	And make the cautery as you please, and according to what you have seen fit; and this is the form of the burn.
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait ij. aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou .ij. se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi .iij. jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrophules are of phlegm and cold moisture, and are not obedient to digestion by medicines, then you must burn off the cautery head, for this is the form, and to do so you must make several incisions on the side of the wound to let out the fumes from the other part; and put the cautery hot on the abscess once, or twice, as much as it is necessary until the abscess bursts; and if the abscess is small, if you put the cautery on according to the quantity of the abscess, and leave it in for two days; and put on wet cotton wool around it until the swelling has gone down. Then cure the wound of abscesses and sutures until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc. Aprés li fai .i. autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	When moisture prevails over the channels of the pores, and even when this comes from a cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be first relieved by solvent medicines; afterwards perform the cautery at the root of the throat, and keep it so that you do not go further than the throat, and do not burn more than is necessary. Afterwards perform another cautery at the joint of the collarbone at the base of the spine; and let the cautery which is called the "claw" remain as it is; and cure the limb as it has been said above until it is healed.
de la toust	When moisture prevails over the channels of the pores, and even when this comes from a cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be first relieved by solvent medicines; afterwards perform the cautery at the root of the throat, and keep it so that you do not go further than the throat, and do not burn more than is necessary. Afterwards perform another cautery at the joint of the collarbone at the base of the spine; and let the cautery which is called the "claw" remain as it is; and cure the limb as it has been said above until it is healed.
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et .i. autre cautere emmi le pis entre .ij. mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When moisture prevails over the pores and the patient has neither fever nor sweating, and the ailment is ancient, if you perform two cauteries on the forcele [jaw] in the front and one between the two nipples; and let the cautery which is called the "claw" remain as it is as it has been said above.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a .xxx., ou enqui entor. Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a .iij. rains selonc ceste forme:	And if you see it, perform the cautery directly on all the cauteries which are called "points" because their shape is like that in the disease of the ears; and let the points be until .xxx., or more bent. Afterwards cure the limb according to what is said above, and let the cauteries be at .iij. rains according to this form.
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And because of that, these cauteries are lighter, for these that you make at .iij. together.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	because of the dislocation of the shoulder.
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterwards, support the patient on their back and chest; then take hold of the thumb which is within the armpit with your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated, if necessary, grasp the cautery which has about an inch of length: thus...
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble .iiij. cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a .iij. ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a .iij. ners:	...and burn the thumb until it reaches the chest, and the burn would come out with three cauteries in total; and for this reason the cautery is made with the cautery which has about two nails, for the figure of cautery is like two nails; and the nerves are according to the fineness of a thread and this is the form of the cautery which has about two nails:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And never is the suture placed upon this nerve because there are seven cauteries there.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	Then put on the cautery, broil the wounds with oil; then rest the patient, and do not move the limb until it is well comforted.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant. Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	And if it is dislocated somewhat, whatever the cause, then make a cautery over the callous of the cautery clamp or the mouth of the cautery. For the joint is closed, and the moisture is strong and the patient is healed.</start_of_turn
dou cautere de pleuresin	of the pleura.
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancient said that we must make for pleuresin cauteries of root of aristologe, and in part thus: take a root of aristologe long, the greatest that thou shalt find, and be dry, and be as great and as long as thy two hands; and the grease in oil, and the mark on the fire, and cauterize. I. Cauterize between the nipple and the collar, and II. Two small cauteries in descending on that which is below the beard; and III. Cauterize between the fifth rib and the twelfth, declining behind a rib. I. Cauterize at the pit of the stomach, and I. Another above the stomach, and I. Between two ribs, and II. Have two ribs below the pit defend the cautery that is between two ribs; and do not press me your hand, but make it open as when smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a .i. raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie. Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	And they say no ancient that no man uses a fire cautery resembling a scraper, and puts it between the ribs, until it comes to this incision; and they jump away because of the pain, as we have said in the incision of the liver. But in this work is fear or the patient dies now, or a fistula comes which cannot be healed.
de la mice	of mice
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse from what we have said concerning the divisions of the cures, and it brings no benefit, then there remain two methods of cautery that are both good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices .iij. cauteres, ou .iiij., en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;	When you treat the disease of the mouse from what we have said concerning the divisions of the cures, and it brings no benefit, then there remain two methods of cautery that are both good.
et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	and another method of cautery is if you fear that the cautery has too many nerves, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and keep the limb in the place where the mouse is, or the patient’s belly comes towards the left side, and let the elevation be such that you support the limb according to the limb, according to the length of the bone, and the cautery should be according to the width of the bone.
Aprés i boute les .ij. ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra .iiij. Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a .iij. ners. Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After that, if the burn is large, do not flame the area any more until the burn is perceived from the other side. Then take away the cautery and there will be three. And if you see that the burn has progressed to the entirety of the burn area, take away the cautery at two-thirds of the burn. After that, cure when the wound has grown for a long time, and this is worth as much as the other cures mentioned before.
de ydropisie	After that, if the burn is large, do not flame the area any more until the burn is perceived from the other side. Then take away the cautery and there will be three. And if you see that the burn has progressed to the entirety of the burn area, take away the cautery at two-thirds of the burn. After that, cure when the wound has grown for a long time, and this is worth as much as the other cures mentioned before.
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes». Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres entor la boude, et .i. sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et .i. sus la mice, et .ij. derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et .i. endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	The cautery is not useful for hydrosis, except in the manner called "asclytes." When you treat it according to the methods we have said in sections, and your cure does not benefit, then you must give it three cauteries around the belly, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the spleen, and two at the back on the spine, and one at the place of the pain; and let the cautery be close to the root of the hair.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After leaving the cautery open for a long time to drain the pus, do not leave the dressing on the patient after the cautery; and healing will be expedited, and both joints will be bound together with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the belly cautery is like a nail which we have before shown; and the olive-shaped one is like that which is shown here
de l’enfleure des piez	of swelling of the parts.
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner. Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	When the parts are swollen with that which is hygro-pneumatic, and are filled with yellow bile, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the thumb between the thumb and the index finger; and keep your hand with the cautery towards you. And do not enter too deeply, for otherwise you will burn the yellow bile, and the cautery should be made in this fashion:
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After that, make two incisions on the thigh; at the tip of the buttock. And let the incisions be long, one of them above the knee and the other below, between the thigh; and leave the incisions open along their length to cure, that they may be healed in peace; after that, perform the other treatments that we have said.
de la menoison	After that, make two incisions on the thigh; at the tip of the buttock. And let the incisions be long, one of them above the knee and the other below, between the thigh; and leave the incisions open along their length to cure, that they may be healed in peace; after that, perform the other treatments that we have said.
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When the solution of the belly comes from cold and moisture, as the retaining and digestive virtue which is the stomach and the intestines is evacuated, and cannot be cured by means of treatment; and you see the patient well suffering and very weak, if you make a great burn on the stomach as it has been said above or a burn of the stomach, at the burn that circulates; and three burns around the abdominal cavity at all times.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	If you see abundant moisture and the patient suffering, perform a cautery on the armpit, and indeed cautery on each side, and three small cauteries on the abdomen below the large one; for the cure is beneficial when there is good aid.

de plaie mal curee	Of a wound that is not properly treated
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure the size or opening, as we have mentioned before, if there be any ailment that cannot be cured except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When there is no opening or fistula, and it is filled with pus and corrupted moisture, if the physician tries in vain to cure it, and maintains that the wound should be cauterized, it is necessary to remove the cautery as soon as it seems to burn, and to insert it into the fistula as much as it will hold, and repeat the cautery until the burnings are cured, when the wound is rigid and corrupted; once, or twice, or three times, according to the amount of matter that must be removed; and beware of nerves that are nearby and of large veins. If the fistula is close to the bladder or intestines, be cautious of these parts, and do not do more harm than necessary; after cauterizing, cure the wound until it is healed, and if the parts are stiff and the matter is ossified along the edges, then cauterize once more; if the matter is not ossified, leave the wound open until it is healed, and corrupt the bone that is beneath, as we mentioned before.

de la hainche	De la hainche.

Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans. de la dolor des jointes	of joint pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain arises from moisture that has spread throughout the limb, and when the pain originates from within the bone, it is called "podagre" properly. de la routure dou syfac	De la routure dou syfac.

tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. And towels that you do not bring up to the cautery, your work is worth nothing. Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre. But the first cauteries are lighter and milder.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in no limb.
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain arises in any limb, whether from injury or from sitting, and the pain persists for a long time, and the medical cure proves useless, then it is recommended to cauterize the area using the cautery known as the "points." The cautery should be performed according to the length of the limb, its breadth, its weakness, its toughness, and its twisting and painfulness. If the first cautery is successful, well and good; if not, repeat the process. Indeed, it is customary to perform the cautery on the area that is closest to the painful area, so that one can make the cauteries until the patient is cured.
de meselerie	When pain arises in any limb, whether from injury or from sitting, and the pain persists for a long time, and the medical cure proves useless, then it is recommended to cauterize the area using the cautery known as the "points." The cautery should be performed according to the length of the limb, its breadth, its weakness, its toughness, and its twisting and painfulness. If the first cautery is successful, well and good; if not, repeat the process. Indeed, it is customary to perform the cautery on the area that is closest to the painful area, so that one can make the cauteries until the patient is cured.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The disease that arises from putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy is not often cured by cautery, but even when it is, the patient often remains sick. If you see the disease in its early stages, take heed and cure it as we have described in the division; do not linger or delay, for if the corruption has spread throughout the body, even repeated cauteries will not be of any avail. Therefore, when cauterizing the head, do so as follows: first cauterize the top of the head, then the front of the head below the eyebrows; then on each side of the nose, and finally on the back of the head below the hairline. Keep your hand over the area being cauterized until the bones are exposed, and until the surrounding tissue has bled out so that the vapors of the humors can escape; then cauterize the mouse according to the situation.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if there is a mixture of moisture everywhere; and it appears openly, if you must use these cauteries that we have mentioned or chief, namely a cautery on the top of the thumb, two cauteries on the spine of the collarbone, three cauteries on the spine of the shoulder, one large on the elbow and one other elsewhere, two on the two thumbs, two on the scapulae, two on the flanks, two on the Achilles tendons, and one on any joint of the hands or feet, and on the pits of the hands; keep away from the nerves that are behind the calcaneus, so that you do not burn them; and never make the cautery on the bones of the heel or the bones of the stomach or the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And the more you make the cautery, the more help you give, and the more benefit you gain; and the patients do not feel pain from the cautery as if they would feel it if it were new, because the flesh is already corrupted. It is necessary that the cautery be large and small according to the members and joints, as you do in handling herbs. After curing the wound several times with flour and honey and other cures until it is healed.
de enfleure	from swelling
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling comes to any limb and is cured by medicines, oils, and plasters, and is not completely healed, then it is done to cauterize on the limb according to the greatness and smallness of the limb; and either the cautery is made at the root of the thumb or at the tip of the ring finger. Then it is cured with ointment until it is healed. And at no time is cautery done on the hand, foot, or back, at the issue of the nerve that makes the limb immobile, or if it is bony swelling. And all this is done without any hindrance if one is skilled in the limb and the issue of the moving nerves around the bone.
de albaras	When swelling comes to any limb and is cured by medicines, oils, and plasters, and is not completely healed, then it is done to cauterize on the limb according to the greatness and smallness of the limb; and either the cautery is made at the root of the thumb or at the tip of the ring finger. Then it is cured with ointment until it is healed. And at no time is cautery done on the hand, foot, or back, at the issue of the nerve that makes the limb immobile, or if it is bony swelling. And all this is done without any hindrance if one is skilled in the limb and the issue of the moving nerves around the bone.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is present, and medicine is of no avail, then it is done to cauterize with a needle once, according to the quantity of the area, until the swelling is bony and has changed colour; then it is cured with flour of times and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and without colocynth and alum, a part of each; and all this is mixed together, and bound up with a bandage, and left to heal until it is healed
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure of chancre by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When the chancre begins, and you see it stop, if you cauterize at the circle [cautery] which appears, all around the circumference of the chancre. And all the wise men say that one should cauterize also in the middle of the chancre; but I do not think that is good, for I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen it happen many times; and the right thing is that it be cauterized around, at the circle which is called the "circle", as we have said concerning the cautery.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot be cured
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When anyone has an ailment called "adubelati," and it lingers without diminishing or due to the excessive production of the disease in the patient when he is decrepit (that is, too old) and there is much blood, or for other reasons; and you see it haste to die: then cauterize around the mouth of a small cautery by pricking; after that leave it in place. For it will haste to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it turn with the entire cautery, if it is hot, cauterize the cautery again so that this is the shape:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And put your hand in the middle of this ailment that is called "adubelati" as long as the cautery has perceived the pain, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels relief in part as the disease progresses. After that cure until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The fire cautery. Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	The fire cautery. Instructs the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times it happens that when a piece of meat is defaced a disease arises which is called "clos" according to our understanding, and is a great thing feared that causes the limb to swell. And the cautery of this disease is in two ways. That is to say, fire cautery and hot water cautery. Fire cautery is that which is done by cauterizing as with a needle a piece of meat just as if it were a pin of wool, and which is done with iron heated to the measure that it can penetrate the abscess of all parts, and that there be subtle margins; after which one puts all around the abscess and holds the hand tightly around the abscess until it comes to the front of the abscess; and one leaves it in place for two days until it begins to discharge pus; then one makes an poultice of bruised wild mallow seeds with wool, and leaves the poultice in place throughout the night, and one closes the abscess tightly and will remove it from its roots. Then one cures the wound by applying pressure until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	If the abscess is converted by the discharge of the flesh, and this happens many times in the hand and the foot, if one must perform hot water cautery; this is in part as follows: take a needle of silver or iron, or a piece of wool, and put it on the abscess and the surrounding area, that is to say, burn the verrucae; then put the needle on so that it reaches all around, then put a little of hot water, and hold the hand firmly, pressing the hand by turning so that the margin of the needle comes to the root of the abscess, and can find the hot water going deep down to the root; and let the patient drink a little of the hot water for an hour; then leave it in place, and it will drain out all at once from all its roots. Do this again until all of the abscess is gone, and then cure the wounds which cause the swelling.
li cure dou trembler	You have not provided any text for me to translate, so I am unable to provide a translation.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When the body trembles from cold, or from a quartan fever or from another, if you make four cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between the shoulder blades, and one cautery at the waist and one on the stomach at the olive cautery; if you leave them on, the trembling will cease and the patient will be cured of the cold.
des pustules puans	When the body trembles from cold, or from a quartan fever or from another, if you make four cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between the shoulder blades, and one cautery at the waist and one on the stomach at the olive cautery; if you leave them on, the trembling will cease and the patient will be cured of the cold.
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Whenever the body is bathed in sweat, or pustules swell up, which come from corrupted matters; if you do this at the first sign, when they appear, make a cautery on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery of fir of myrtle, from which the point should be grasped by the fire, or of aristegall root, or by the cautery of lentils. And never should you cauterize them at the beginning when they appear, but only in this manner, and they will not be cut through, but will be broken up by the excess from which they come, and will be healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	When the artery is cut, there is often great bleeding from the artery at the wound which comes from the surgeon, or from the incision of the abscess, or from the cautery of the limb, and similar things; and it is a mournful thing to watch.</start_of_turn>
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And whenever this happens, if you are in a hurry to put your thumb on the wound of the vein, and you strain too much without calming your thumb, and no blood comes out anymore; then take olive oil cauteries of various sizes and make them red; then press down, that is, large or small as it is suitable for the wound and the limb in which the artery is passing, and put the cautery on that vein or hold your thumb there, and hold the cautery as long as it is necessary without letting it go.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if there is bleeding again when you remove your thumb from the vein, and the cautery is finished, take hold of another cautery that is on the fire immediately.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do this one after the other until the limb is restored; and beware that you do not damage the nerve that is nearby, and that no other harm comes upon the patient; and take notice that when without displacement of an artery, it is not possible to fill it up properly even when the artery is large, except by one of the three methods that we have mentioned: or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not otherwise treated, or by strong ligation of thread, or by medicines placed upon it that have power to restore blood flow. And let it be firmly held in place afterward.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever brings about the restoration of the limb violently with cloths or with the laying on of burning things, or other similar things, if it does not prove helpful, does harm.</start_of_turn>
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if there is no other remedy and there is no medicine present, if necessary put your two fingers on the wound of the vein as we have said, and keep them in place until the bleeding stops; and do not move the limb, but moisten it with cold water often so that it may be cold to the touch as long as the limb is frozen and swollen and resting; and make incisions in front of this where cautery and medicines must be applied.</start_of_turn>
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Ci encourag li secons livre des cures de taille.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	Now we have said or previously in the first chapter that every disease in which it is necessary to perform cautery of fire, or of applied medicine, and the methods, causes and instruments, and forms of cauteries; and in this chapter we shall speak of those matters in this way that we find them more conveniently in this chapter through this way.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus, as I begin this chapter, it is necessary, my son, to learn that in this chapter there is more peril and fear than in the previous chapters of the cauteries, and for this reason it is necessary to take greater precautions.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you that you do not undertake madness. For many people come to cures in various ways. If they come from those who have suffered so greatly from their illness that they move lightly from fear of their disease, and from the greatness of their malice; of these things we must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And of these there are some who make you understand, saying: "Wait, I am ready"; and the illness is desperate. It does not suffice for me that you yield to those who come to you who have this manner, but put more great caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not carelessly speak more than reasonably of what you are certain of, and of what you have taken and lost; and use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your patients so that salvation is either obtained or converted; and this will help you to acquire good renown, glory, and memory that lasts long.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, our lords, you must understand and rejoice, and if you yearn to be inspired by the holy inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selon ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’à piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.
dou chief plein d’aigue	Or I have commanded thee this chapter by dividing it into chapters, according to that which is before or the chapter of cautery, that I have commanded thee from the chief to the feet, forasmuch thou shalt find more easily that of which thou hast need.
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Saiches that this ailment comes out many times as soon as the child is born, and when the bail is strained too strong the head of the child; and never comes from any other cause save that which does not go away
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen such a disease vanish except in childhood, and in all that I have heard, the patient always died; for this reason I believe that it is better to leave the work in parts rather than to cure it.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I once saw a child in whom the bone was completely split with pain, and the head grew so much that it could not bear; and I believed that the moisture was so great that it would kill the patient, and when it is collected between the bone and the flesh, between the marrow and the bone; and the work is such that if the moisture is between the marrow and the bone, and the incision is small, you must make a wide cut; and as long as the moisture remains, the form is like that of a spasm
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper, and the incision is larger, if you make two incisions in the shape of a cross, following this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	If moisture swells the bone, and the sign that you see the head of the bone protrude from the chest, and it sharpens when you press it with your hand from within, and it does not return: if you suspect that the head of the bone is fractured, you must make two incisions as follows:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. de reume	When the bone is fractured or the vein is opened, and the cavity is filled with liquid, do as you please; but beware that you do not cover the artery; let the blood flow freely, for if the patient dies from excessive bleeding and evacuation of moisture.

Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When ancient dropsy comes with acute catarrh, because of the tears and the choleric humours in the temples and the ancient sode are lost and similar things, and it is treated by means of medical cures and all that does not benefit, except for the cauterization of the arteries of the temples.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And thus the method of extracting them is that if the patient makes the hair of his temples grow long, and understands the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is not put back as quickly as in some men who are too cold; and if it is put back, the patient must raise his head from some covering, then rub the limb with no rough cloth, and pour cold water over it until the artery opens clearly; then take the spatumile, which is its shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. And thus the method of extracting them is that if the patient makes the hair of his temples grow long, and understands the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is not put back as quickly as in some men who are too cold; and if it is put back, the patient must raise his head from some covering, then rub the limb with no rough cloth, and pour cold water over it until the artery opens clearly; then take the spatumile, which is its shape, and gently stretch the leather until you see the artery, then pull it up tightly with tweezers, and cut off the hair at the root. For if it is not cut off, it will not jump out without pain in all its parts.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And pull out blood from the groin to the elbow, just as much as is necessary; and if the artery is large, it is convenient to bind it with two strong threads of silk, so that no blood will appear in front of the wound, and let the blood drain naturally; then cut away the surplus that is between the two threads in that place, and if you see that, if you wish, you can cauterize with a cautery needle until the hair is cut off; and that is the best remedy, if the patient has no fever and is of a warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the fire cautery is useful for finishing off moisture: because of this it is of more use against moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For it is useful to extract the arteries that are filled with much cotton and put on well-made bandages; and when you remove them, if you are cured of dry medicines that cause the growth of hair and bandages, as long as you are sane; and if you do not have a staunch for the artery as you should when you cover with cautery, or you use the hand of vitriol and strain it from your hand, which is without stain; and if you do not have that, if you must remove the limb, you must do so until it is frozen, and rise the limb with cold water until it stops, and strain it as it should be strained; and what is more tender and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this cautery cutting through a third part, but the cutting should be well spaced to ward off more length of heat.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too tense, it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	The fire cautery must have between the joints a space of one inch. Then, when you have marked the area with needles, let the loop of the forceps burn over until it reaches the bone, and grasp the vein with the forceps; and keep the bones separated from each other because they are not soldered by this cautery in any way. This is the form of the fire cautery.
des larmes	The fire cautery must have between the joints a space of one inch. Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When no acute cautery is used, you see the pupils tense and small, and the vision blurred; and the hair on the head prickles, and there is great pain, and the patient coughs; then drool from these accidents as from those matters and this cautery does not come from many veins, but from many wounds.
