de l’estoupement des oreilles	From the swelling of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that causes swelling of the ears is one of three things: grains, or pus, or stone or other foreign bodies; or seed, as in cases of peas, beans, or barley; or a flowing liquid as in the case of fever and chills and other things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When there is a stone or other foreign body in the ear that does not fit into the ear, do not put the ear into the sun. If you see the stone, if no violet oil or mastic oil comes from it, then prepare for extraction; and let him vomit, and stop the bleeding from the nose when he vomits, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and extend the ear downwards. Many times the pain will go away by this cure; and if it does not go away, prepare for extraction with needles, as this is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If the stone comes out by itself, that is good; if not, prepare for extraction with small needles of double curvature; and if it does not come out by this, take a pinch of the flesh and tear a part of the ear very little, and stop the bleeding that comes from the wound with wax if necessary; then the pain will go away, for many times it comes out by itself as we have said; and if it does not come out in this way, take hold of the flesh around the wound and press on the stone or whatever it is, and the pain will go away.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If these things do not suffice, if you are in a hurry to make an incision at the ear base as well as at the apex of the chalazion vein, and if there is spasm, do not hesitate to make the incision first at the front of the head; then draw the patient’s head between your hands and turn the ear downwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear, at the fatty tissue or bone depending on which is easier; and let the vein bleed out as much as necessary, and evacuate the pus from the wound until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is grains that are swollen and inflamed, administer extraction; and if it cannot be extracted, administer sponge-rubber according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But make no incision until you think the grain is moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many attempts; then extract it with tweezers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned.</start_of_turn>
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	When the ear aches, the patient should immediately apply a warm compress to the ear and fill it with cotton wool. If the pain persists, take many small stones according to the length of the ear canal and push them in with tweezers; put the patient’s ear to the fire; and put one or two stones into the ear, and pull out the pieces from the other side, and burn another stone on the stone that is in the ear; and do this until the pain is gone. If you see that the pain has gone, take the tweezers and grasp one of the stones in the ear, and burn the other stone as long as the joint is painful; then put in the rest of the stones until the pain is gone, as we have said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the tooth, if it is of small size, as with a flea and other things, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is of large size, we must feel it, and it is the easiest thing to extract the tooth that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms from the ear, when you have cured it as we have said in the division or treated with distillations, the cure does not help, if you look at the ear in the sun: if there are no worms, if you see only subtle wounds, and if you do not see any, take the tweezers which are like this:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the swelling of the ears.
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien. de la gresle	De la gresle.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times come papers of pus from things that seem greasy in their form and hardness; for this is the disease called "granulin", and is an assembly of large moisture in the papere of the belly and of the feet; the work is such: take warning if the granulin moves from one side to the other, and this is a light thing to know; then make a large incision, then strip away the soft part lightly, then take tweezers and grasp. If you do not grasp it in the right direction, you will not see the papere; and if the wound is large, if the assembly has a costure, and cure until it is healed; and if it is small, do not use force, for it will be restored as soon as the swelling subsides and the pus is drained.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the granulin descends into the ear towards the upper part, if you reverse the papere, and bring the granulin to a few tweezers, grasp and press from one side to the other; and if the papere is loosened by the incision, this will cause no harm; and when the granulin is grasped, if you leave the dirty oil, cure the body of that which is drained until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the pus.
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	The fat of the ox is enclosed in paper tissues and this has happened more to the common folk than to the nobles; for the mucus runs from their eyes and they are unable to behold the sunlight for fear that the tears will run from their eyes; and for this reason they lie with their faces down and sleep, and their paper tissues are soaked with moisture that swells and appears covered in the fat of the ox which breaks out in the oil. And when you press the limb to your chest and feel the fat between your thighs.

The manner of the work is that the patient puts his head in order; then take one sheet of linen and make a circle around the quantity of fat in the chest part, and put it on; and press on your thighs from one side and the other, so that the fat is assembled together in the circle; then make in the middle of the moisture at the spiddle trenching a wound not more large than the wound we make to the vein; and make the leather firm as long as you see the fat; and in many positions comes fat from the wound, according to the shape of a white piece of fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract the thick piece of marrow between your thighs at the waist, and twist your hand to the right and to the left as much as possible; and keep that you do not touch the wound, that you do not come near to the oil until it is finished, that you do not stain it.

And if there are such persons who scratch themselves and put on things to corrupt that moisture which is dried up. Then cure it until it is healed. des poilz des papieres	hair of papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai. de la porriture de l’oil	of the corruption of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses. And the way of working in this is that you make this suture and dry the flesh, and put inside some lint, and leave it until it is healed; and do not do anything but use in the treatment of this things that dry and restrain. Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your treatment is that you must take care that it does not heal differently from the way it was before; and this work that we have said is not fierce except for addressing this disease, that it does not come back differently from the way it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	Of the cauldron that comes in the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	Of the cauldron that comes in the oil, this disease which is caused by moisture is called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental. The accident comes from wound and fracture and cautery and things of that kind; and the way of the work in this is that if you take an awl, because it has two threads, and the hook is in the cauldron, and it makes the left upper lip split so that the thread of the vein is split into two pieces in about three quarters of the cauldron; then the cauldron is placed below at the whole of the awl, and the handle has one large spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound returns as it should, that is good; if not, take a scraper and put it into the fracture, and twist the wound, and make two incisions or cut through the middle of the wound; and if there are three incisions from each angle of the incision that you have made, or if you make an angle so that when they are assembled, the figure is as that of a letter which has not "j. griesche"; then bind that cauldron, according to the quantity of its cost and moisture, of that which will soothe the wound, and then join the two severed parts, and bind them with a thread of linen; then apply the remedies that we have said of the mollifying medicines and bandages, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	If the sickness comes from a fracture or a suture or from cautery, then it must be made that you make a clean incision all around the hairs of paper; and as for what is above, separate between the two books of a thumb, as I have said; and must be done according to the form of the sickness, for it is diverse in form, and the learned men appear to know everything from head to foot how to restore the figure to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what is suitable for the work and for the instruments in various arrangements.
dou soudement de la papiere	If the sickness comes from a fracture or a suture or from cautery, then it must be made that you make a clean incision all around the hairs of paper; and as for what is above, separate between the two books of a thumb, as I have said; and must be done according to the form of the sickness, for it is diverse in form, and the learned men appear to know everything from head to foot how to restore the figure to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what is suitable for the work and for the instruments in various arrangements.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	If this fracture has occurred at the shoulder joint in such a manner that the limb hangs suspended with the palm downwards, and is unable to move or perform its natural functions, if it must be that you extract the bone from the palm of the hand, and elevate it upwards; and that the edges be bound together, as long as the surrounding skin is not too tight and does not tear the oil; and that your incision, which you have made to reassemble, be slight, so that the limb returns to its natural shape; and that all that has been reassembled be bound together, and that no more oil be added to the wound, but only a little sweet water and vinegar; and after that put between the limb and the oil a cloth of linen, and cover with oily wool in abundance; and finally put on a bandage of wool and other soothing things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	De l’ungle de l’oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Saiches that the nail is in two manners: it is nervous and seems like tough fat, and another which is not very nervous, but seems like white moisture frozen, that when it is touched with iron and is cooked through, there are pinpricks; and both seem to swell towards the great tear, and rise up so much that they cover the whole eye and the light and movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is that the patient places his hand in his bosom, then grasps the eyes; and keep your hand on his wrist, and then break the nail with pinpricks of small double curvature, and stretch it upwards; then take a needle, and put in one hair of horse, or of sheep, or of beef, and one strong thread; and double the point of the needle once and fix it in the nail, and pierce through the whole needle, and tie the nail with a thread and stretch it upwards, and support all around the nail the cost of the nail that surrounds the nail-bed and the hair to the hair just as far as the chief, and then close the remaining part in the root of the tear with all the small forces, and leave the natural tear or the tear itself; and in no way stretch the nail only with the needle and the thread, as we have said; then support all around the nail the surrounding area that is this form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And keep that the sponge does not touch the fleshy cloth and break it, and that the needle does not pierce it; and after the incision, pour oil a little ball of butter, and give him a decoction of alum, and leave it until the other side; then cure what is left of it until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous, and you cannot push back the needle, and the thread does not pass through, many times it is cured of this semblance of nail; and as I have said in the division, if you see it covered, if you pour oil on the patient, and take the sponge more slight in this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And withdraw the nail gradually, and if you see that it does not decrease point and that the edge is pressing, if you distill from your mouth into the oil decoction of alum and red alum and butter, and pour oil until the other side; then repeat the other work as before, until it is completely healed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing opposes you in oil, as with an abscess, then milk, and cure the abscess first while it is healthy, then resume the work as before, while it is healthy.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	If there appears fat floating in the oil at night, with great swelling, if you suspend it in vinegar, and cut off a part and not the whole, that blood does not rise; then distill in the red oil of colera, which is made from litharge.</start_of_turn>
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that comes from the navel.
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	The eye of some men never bursts; cover the navel and bind on the papers and torment them with fire, and it seems like a rose of thorns; and when the patient puts his head in his stomach, then do the eyes burst, and all that heat has a reasonable cause for this, and the support has force; then take the first heat and go through it all to the end, and keep only the fumes left at the work. And let the incision be as small as possible, as we have said in the incision of the vein, and have little force of the hand to move the bone.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	When the incision is complete and the bone is all taken out, if you use cold oil of safflower or you distill it and similar corrosive medicines, and put on the oil cotton with eggshell, so that it should be well protected; and if it does not stay, and the patient vomits, and you doubt the protection, if you leave the oil and cure the abscess with calming things that protect the protection; then return to your work until it is healed, and when you do the charges are added to the oil in this way.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But it is necessary to nourish the cure with a weak oil of natural origin; and in an accident, in the work of fire; and do not burn your hand in any of these works until you see that the limb is suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	From the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	The veins of the eyes are red and covered with oil, and tolerate the gaze of the patient and irritate the oil always. The physician should therefore take care at first that the patient rests his head still, then suspend the veins all around as he deems appropriate, and do so cautiously: for in this matter there is great force; there is no other disease more fierce than madness; therefore one must handle it cautiously.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And two veins by degrees in one limb according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then suspend these veins gradually by degrees in one limb according to this form:

de la fistule de l’oil	And if you are unable to collect all of this in that hour, make a poultice on the oil of soothing things to ease the pain of the eyes, and leave it until the pain is relieved and is secure from after-pain; then begin again according to this manner which is before, until it is healed; and that is the way of the forces.

The mire so named "arissati" fistula: when you cure it by cautery and medicine with burning water, as I have said before, and it is not completely healed, if there is any moisture remaining in it, then you must make an incision on the after-pain, there or wherever it must measure, and drain out all the moisture, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is fractured, and you see the corruption and darkness, if the limb has all the signs, it is called an "aspre chief"; and is made like a nail, that is, a fractured bone, and is pointed out like a lime when it is in this form.

se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the limb is swollen and chares do not appear, and the bone is fractured, and remains so for eighty days, and does not heal and is not to be sutured, and any other remedy does not come, save to restore the fistula to its natural place: uncover the bone a second time with iron, and with sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered take hold of the limb as described above, and the bone should be bent at two angles, and the limb should be reduced to its natural shape as you see here.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide. de l’issue de l’oil	Then place your thumb on the bone below the armpit, and wipe your hand with oil. When the wound opens all the way and does not cause discomfort in the chest, neither does it cause any reduction, if you are to bind the patient; then the same, then apply a compress or bandage in a counterclockwise direction to draw out the wound, then apply oil. de la bowe de l’oil	De la bowe de l’oil.
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	The bow of oil.
des aigues de l’oil	Des aigues de l’oil.
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.
