Se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After a little rest, if the water comes back in the second time, put the force with the instrument, and when it is firmly fixed and does not move, grasp the almagda lightly by circling your hand a little and a little; and then put back in the water a little of the previously extracted liquid, and remove the oil from within. Then put on the oil-soaked compress or gauze with abundant egg yolks, and tie with the oil-soaked bandage. We and those who are with us put on a woolen brochet with abundant egg yolks.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter the oil because there are parts of bone that have too thick the hairs, then you must take the instrument which is called the «alberit», which is like this in shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce then only the conjunctive, do not linger too much in the process, but make it subtle; and when you are finished, the patient will perceive immediately the coming of sleep, as we have said; and when the work is finished, the patient will experience a deep sleep on his back for one and a half hours; and let him rest peacefully, and take nourishment, and do not move his head to the right or left, and bind him as he lies until three quarters; then release him in this same house, uncover his face, and let him see nothing; and then put him back in the same position until seven quarters; and do not let him do anything else until you have finished the treatment or the incision, but make sure to feed him, for his pain will increase greatly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And when the swelling has gone down, take away the oil before the seven quarters; and bring in that which quiets the abscess; and when it is quiet, loosen the face and put on a little ointment to cover any raw spots; and keep it bound in this same house. And then go out of the house and come in again, and he will recover in his case; and do not let anyone touch his things in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us from Iraq, who told us that in his land when a person is in pain, they make a great meal and perceive the pain as a joy; but we have never seen or read about anything like that in our land or in the books of the ancients; and it is a new thing to us
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the signs of the shapes of an almond, for those who do not know them; and they are like peas in rows:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And their heads are of this same subtlety, and their backs in two angles like a bow.
de la char sor le neis	like the head of a spear from the neck.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Sometimes births or deaths of various hairs occur, for there are some which seem like scorpions with teeth; and if there are such or if there is hair entangled with blood-red color, or if there is hair of grey color like bone. In this case of those hairs which are grey and not entangled, it is to be known that you must make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and cover his nose, and spit out the seed at those hairs, and pull them out; then take what you have in your hand to support the subtle gut of a part, until you are sure that that hair is entirely bony.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If nothing remains to hold it, if the opening has been made with too little force, if nothing settles; and if it swells without stopping, or if it hangs loose, or if it is an abscess, then grasp it firmly as if it were possible; and if it is a malignant abscess, hasten and cauterize it while it is not stained and all the pus has gone, then throw or pull out the contents easily and with speed or vinegar.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If it does not swell, and moisture comes up to the palate, the teeth that were sound; if moisture does not pierce as it should, teeth that are loose in the bone below, behold the instruments do not come out by force: therefore it must be that you drink a large thread of silk, and keep hold with the hands, and put between each knot no more than; and put the patient’s limb under the thread at the armpit, and stretch until it comes through the mouth; and many times do the children do this, and it is a light matter for one who has seen it done; then hold the chief that comes from the armpit with one hand, and the other chief that comes from the mouth with the other hand, and take the one after the other as we are or as the thread is. Do this until you are sure that the knot has not corrupted the tooth, then pull out the thread, wipe the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian balsam, and put it back in place as before; do this two or three days, until the pus has corroded all that is remaining of the tooth; and then put out or remove a cautery again for several days until it is healed, and if there is any need of sedatives, use them; and this is the form of the instrument for extracting the tooth, as we distill oils and medicines or not.</start_of_turn>
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And be it of silver or of gold, resembling an overlarge lamp, if like a cord; and if you see it, make a closed cord, and the instrument will be flat to purge the tooth; and have one hand on the chief to hold it when oil or no liquid is being burned.</start_of_turn>
de la char sor le neis	From the armpit on the neck.
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times there arises at the root of the neck a disease which is called "telul", and it grows and becomes very great all of a sudden, so that it is visible to see; and for this reason it is commanded that you should begin to compress it at the beginning, and break the bone thoroughly, then apply the cautery or burning medicine; and if you delay in compressing it when it is great, if you take hold of it firmly, from a dark color to a pale hue, if you do not touch it with iron, for it is a thorny abscess, for when you touch it even once, there comes great harm to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of dark color, you can see that you can easily compress it, if you leave the patient and compress it without fear, and cure the limb of dry and restraining things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the neck is cut and bound.
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	When solutions of continuation arise in these cartillages, it proves useful for some people. It is therefore not to be omitted, if one sees that the wound is fresh throughout its extent; and then add three fingers to a bolster and hold it until it is healed. If the fingers are already detached at one end and the other, if one must support all the parts of the limb until they bleed, and then assemble the fingers to a bolster, and strain, and sprinkle gunpowder on gunpowder of dragon, and burn; and put upon the gunpowder a piece of replacement of great or other solid replacement that adheres, and leave it until it bleeds out by itself, and then cure it until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of making the bolster is that you assemble the solution: either with needles, as we have said in the belly bolster; or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of the detachments of the fingers.
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At the hands of a master, the book has teeth like sharp grains of wheat, minor and greater; thus it is right that you must break the teeth, open each socket, and take them as pincers and grasp in the front part; then apply the paste after the incision of the vitreous membrane, until it is dry; and then remove it easily, and cure the part with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	From the root of the gums.
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times blood appears on the teeth of the gums, which are often called "albules"; if you hold them steady and grasp their root, and let the blood flow out or the blood clot; then put out the vitreous membrane, or other drying and restraining powders; and if the gum comes back after the incision, and this happens many times, if you grasp it a second time and cauterize: if it does not come back even after the cautery; these are the signs of the instruments that cover it.
des sordens	Des sordens.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Once are assembled at the chief of the teeth, in the mouth between the gums, teeth which are lazy and dull; and never are the teeth black and yellow and hollow, until the corruption comes to the gum, and they are biting; if you make the patient sit between your hands, and his head is straight, and open the teeth or the gums open, until nothing remains; and then make black and green, and yellow and other spots, until they are whole; and if that has happened at the first reason, it is good; if that has not happened, if you repeat the second and third time, until you have done everything; and the teeth that have to be extracted have various forms of instruments to remove them, as that which the work shows, because the raisers of the teeth which one must withdraw have other forms than those which one must put between the teeth; and these forms and others are seen with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you later withdraw as much as you wish, because it must not make me do it; for it is a substance that is very bitter, therefore we have no excuse for neglecting to remove it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	When the patient is constrained to endure, if you are certain that the pain will depart, many times the pain will depart from the patient; and care that it is neither too great nor too small, and make the patient groan; and although it does not depart, as long as the patient endures, because we have already done it for these scoundrels; and when you are well certain that the pain will depart, then you must lead the patient to vomit violently to protect the teeth from all parts; then the muscles are to be flexed at the shoulder and elbow joints, as much as they are well displaced, and then fix the elbow firmly; and keep the patient’s head in your hand between your knees, and hold it firmly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After that, stretch the tooth directly toward the cheek, and if it does not move, take no instruments and hold the tooth loosely from the front part; and move it as you did before. And if the tooth is perceived and mixed, if you cover it with cloths, the gum or the tooth itself will be damaged; and if the subtle strain has tenailles, do not break by straining; and you must moisten thoroughly over the gum to soften the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And take care well that you do not break it, and that you leave some part of it, and return to the patient with the greater pain of the first. And take care that you do not do what the ignorant layman do, who break their bones every time without any care, and do not bring anything but this which we have told you; but they bring all sorts of misfortunes from the root of this great disease because of the bones that remain broken, or from the bone that is broken, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is broken, wash the blood of wine or vinegar and salt; and if there is any discharge, that often happens, if you apply the juice of vitriol to it; and if that does not suffice, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments, indeed mute them at first, whether with long points and broad handles, that they do not double in number when you draw the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of large size if they do not bend while drawing, and be of iron well made, and be tipped with teeth to hold.</start_of_turn>
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth.</start_of_turn>
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root is drawn out at the root, if you must put out the moist cotton in the burrow. That is to say, towards the inside or towards the outside, until the wound is softened; and then hold the forceps that are called “algefri,” for in this way the head of the shoulder seems like a beak of a sparrow; and be made as with a file and that is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not suffice to withstand all these tensions, if you must uncover the bark entirely around the root, and place the instrument which is called "althali," which is to say a palainche, from which it is known.
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be strong and firm so that it does not break me, and if the root leaps up by this, that is good; if not, if you aid me with all your instruments, from which these forms will come afterwards.
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you use this instrument which has teeth, from which it is known.
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other instruments which are before the teeth, and this instrument which appears like a great clamp, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And other instruments which are before the teeth, and this instrument which appears like a great clamp, of which this is the form: let it be known that this instrument is so strong that it cannot break, and its jaws like those of instruments for teeth; and with other instruments which are not mentioned here; the master surgeon will himself find the instrument which is appropriate for each case, according to what his work and the disease demonstrate, for there are many diseases for which the old methods do not teach any instrument because of their diversity; and if it breaks at the root of the bone or any other bone, or if it moves, if it seeks these instruments that it must be used, as I have said, and to aid it with gestures, for this is its form.
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let it be known that it must be strong and well-held to hold the bone, that it does not escape, but that it can hold and restrain; and then restore the limb of medicine that is appropriate for this, and if there is inflammation in the bone, and it is small, if the grasp has all these instruments:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears does not follow the natural curve, and the form is bad, even in women of fair complexion, if one should know that it is necessary to extract it since it cannot be saved or comforted: then one must remove it; and if it is close to the tooth, take hold of this instrument which is like a small beak, and if it is of iron without a groove at the top.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the socket often swells and swells up in the hands for the duration of the tooth, and because of this one does not move the others, and if it appears one can limber it if one files a piece of the file to the shape of this:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is like when one files nails; and while filing the tooth slightly, if it does not move too much, when the work is finished at the end there is no rasp, and when it is dense enough it bites the tongue, so if one limps the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not bite the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth loosen.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the teeth loosen, whether by percussion or biting, and the patient is unable to press against what annoys them, you must treat them with restrictive medicines, which is of no avail; for if you order them to be restrained with a golden thread, because the silver thread becomes green and is harmful, but the gum does not move at all; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you see that the teeth are aligned, if you take a loop of thread and pass it twice between the two front teeth, then put the teeth between the front teeth, if there are one or more, as long as you see them steadily up to the adjacent tooth; and then resume the coverage up to the part where you began, and strain your hand steadily and cautiously, until it does not move; and if your thread is tied to the root of the tooth if it cannot escape. Then close the teeth with the thread and reassemble them, and put them back between the adjacent teeth, and put them so that they do not touch the tongue; and then leave them so tight as they can remain stable, and if they slip or the thread breaks, if the strain of another thread; if it lingers and will serve just as well, and that is the form of the teeth and the arrangement of the front teeth and the back teeth, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth aches, if you put it back in its place, fresh from fresh, as we have said; and let nothing interfere that is not wise and soothing, and never make the shape of a tooth of whalebone, and put it back in the place where the defect is, and strain it as we have said, and keep it tight and serve for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	De coper lou liien de la lengue.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	The tongue hangs limp by the side of the jaw; or sometimes from the birth of the limb; or by the violence of a deep wound. The patient must open the mouth widely and stretch out his tongue. Then grasp the large nerve that comes from the root of the tongue, while the tongue is displaced from its place, and if there is any delay or if it does not yield, and it is a sign of a wound, if you stop the bleeding and grasp the limb widely; and keep the wound from becoming too deep, for the artery that comes from the root. And when you have done this, if the limb becomes pale and soft, or cold, remove the clot; and if it does not go away, cauterize with the blunt cautery, which is good for this; and then treat it with another remedy until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see pus color or black or hard, if the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a sore; and if it is declining to swell, and there is moisture, if it evacuates the clot, and you wipe with a fine sponge, and deliver from a part and from another; and if it does not go away from your work, if you put on a broiled vitriol until it is dry, and then return to your work until you have finished all the work; then lift the limb easily and gently, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Des apostemes de la gorge.
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	There are often boils in the throat which are called "godath," and they are often accompanied by swelling of the tonsils. And when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take care: if they are boils of small size and little pus, do not touch them with iron. And if they are red and the root is large, do not touch them with iron, even though you must remove the pus; but leave them until they are dead, and then you will remove them, or they will break by themselves; and if they are white in color and the root is slight, if you have brought the instrument to cover, but look first that the boil rests peacefully and is calmed. Then have the patient sit in the sun, and his shoulders relaxed, and cover his mouth and grasp his hands between his, and press the tongue down towards the instrument, as it is formed; and let it be of silver or gold, just like a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	... and you see the boil, take the sponge and press it into the abscess, and hold it firmly for more than you wish; and do not pull out any hair with your fingers, then put the cover on the instrument, as it is formed, which looks like a force; and if the chief is crooked, and one place is higher than the other, and they are very painful, and is made of iron or tin.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	If you do not have this instrument present, if you can manage with tenailles, know that this is the shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	If you do not have this instrument present, if you can manage with tenailles, know that this is the shape: cut an almond from one side and the other; and when you have grasped one almond, grasp the other in the same manner, and after the incision, gargle the patient with hot water, hot and easy, and if blood appears, gargle the patient with hot water, or extract pomegranate seeds or rue marigold, or similar things, until the bleeding stops; then cure as long as it is healed; and never again does an abscess appear in the throat except for the two almonds, if you grasp them just like the two almonds always.</start_of_turn>
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was not in the throat, namely an abscess of little size; and I had her hold her throat very close, so that the woman could not breathe through the passage that was blocked, and could not eat or drink, and died because she fainted. And the abscess was so high that it had forced out two teeth from their sockets. I therefore had her take two doses of opium, then I forced out a great portion of saliva; then I repeated the process in the other socket where the abscess was. I closed the mouth and squeezed the tongue; then I put the opium back into these abscesses, and closed one part, and only a little blood escaped; and I extracted the passage from the throat and as she began to drink water and then wine, and did not stop spitting out blood from that abscess for a long time; and the abscess returned to its place and filled the space that I had evacuated, until it was almost as big as before; then I bound it and cauterized it inside the throat: and that was the end of the matter; and I departed from those parts, and only God knows what happened to her after I left.
de l’uve	De l’uve.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	From the navel.
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is a hair or something put on the medicine, as the hairs of a spoonful, put the instrument on all the medicine above the navel; and the patient should be sitting on his cost, so that he salivates and the mucus comes out of his mouth from the medicine inside, if it does not go down to the throat, and the coughing; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it on the navel, the amount of half an hour, until you see it limp and the biting of the medicine is appeased; and if you see that, take cotton and wrap it over any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and withdraw the instrument with all the cotton in the cautery, until the cotton is burned on the navel; and do this often, until the cautery is perfect, then leave it dry and clean the cautery after three or five days. And if you must restart the medicine, if you restart it, and after the cautery wipe around the navel with cotton wool, and cover what is around the medicine; and be raised with cold water, and be cured of hiccups until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision, for it is treated by fumigation according to this method. Take camomile, rue, origanum, ivy, cloves, and vinegar and assemble them all or any of them in a pot. Put some oil in it and boil. The pot must be well sealed with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot is a tool that should be hooked according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	This cure is safer than incision, for it is treated by fumigation according to this method. Take camomile, rue, origanum, ivy, cloves, and vinegar and assemble them all or any of them in a pot. Put some oil in it and boil. The pot must be well sealed with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot is a tool that should be hooked according to this method.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it has happened at the throat of an os or fish bone, or nothing; so it is therefore necessary that you should perceive what you see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you see the thing; and what does not appear to you and is returned to the throat, do make the patient vomit the sickness as soon as the meat is cooked in the stomach; by chance if the thing is expelled by vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and join the sponge to the thread and then transfix it. And when it comes back, if it is swollen, then draw it out again; and if it does not come out by itself, take a hook according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument curve at the head if it can more easily enter the gorge, and keep the head raised up; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, that all may go well, do not push the bone inwards; and it is better that the patient move the instrument, because it is either stiff or the matter is putrefying; if the epiglottis is swollen, or if it is forced out with all the instrument equally, as much as it is forced.
de la sansue de la gorge	And let the instrument curve at the head if it can more easily enter the throat, and keep the head raised up; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, that all may go well, do not push the bone inwards; and it is better that the patient move the instrument, because it is either stiff or the matter is putrefying; if the epiglottis is swollen, or if it is forced out with all the instrument equally, as much as it is forced.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Never is medicine enough, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when that does not help, then look at the patient’s throat in the sunlight, and press the tongue to the instrument that I have told you of. And if you see the swelling, if it has gone all the way to the little tonsils, or if there are tense bits that are worth as much. And if that is not worth it, if you take a mouthful of vinegar, and put it in the patient’s throat, and then take away or swallow the vinegar; and if the patient still has pain, take a full dose of cold water, and rinse the mouth, and swallow, and move the tongue often; and if the swelling is severe, spit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	If she does not yield as we have said, if you suffocate the patient with asafoetida, with the instrument that I have mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will make sense. And the manner of fumigation is that you take one pot or there are charcoal pieces, and put the dressing over a coverlet felt in the middle, and in that hole is the head of the instrument; then you pour out your fumigation, and the patient puts the chief of the cane in his mouth, closes his mouth, so that the smoke does not go out, but comes out until the nausea; and the nausea will now cease, and if she does not yield, repeat the fumigation many times; and offer the patient thirst, and make him drink dirty and foul things, and do not drink water; and thus will she be forced to yield by this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument is thus that, as we have mentioned, when it is seen, it resembles tongs with teeth to enter the throat; and it has the shape of a beak of heron, and it has a rough lime, so that whatever it grasps, it cannot let go; and thus is the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	the surgeon of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	The wounds of boils are diverse in perforation and size; for some are similar to their root, and those that hold moisture. Others are caused by the bones or are fixed to the flesh. For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and those of the bones of the joints are different from those that occur in the tissues.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	If the abscess does not need to be pierced, as long as it lies according to its companion; but if there are some that must be pierced when they are hard, and do not die according to their companion, like an abscess that comes from a joint; for when an abscess comes from a joint, and it is left as it is until it is rotten, by chance if the tendon and nerve of the joint are ruptured, which is the cause of contraction in that limb. Or if the abscess comes from the main part of the limb, and you delay the perforation until it is measured, it will reach the main part of the limb; or if it comes from the foundation, if the perforation is not done as soon as it is measured, it will remain unhealed.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	It is necessary that you take out the pus of the abscess that is dead according to its companion; when the pain is calmed, the swelling has gone down, the redness and the heat have disappeared, the throbbing and the pain in the head of the abscess, and other signs; and that you make the perforation or drain the abscess more dependent on the abscess, and the place where it is; and that the perforation is long enough for the abscess that is at the hands or feet, or in the joints and nerves and arteries, and for all the bones that are equal or there is no swelling.

Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	See here the forms of the instruments that are introduced into the body, and there are three kinds: great, middle, and small; and there are four quarters which are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb", and there are three kinds: great, middle, and small, to surround the fistulas.

dou chancre	And draw out the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the cause of this that is causing it, and bandage the limb.
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division concerning the signs of the chancre, and how one must treat it with medicine, and how one must shun the treatment of fire; and we say that the chancre is like a tumor in the marrow, and has great caution in its treatment, and the old men say that when a chancre is in the bone or can be pulled out like a tumor in the marrow, and in the flesh, and similar things, and it must be completely eradicated when it is in its beginning; but when it is great and old, if one cannot approach it, for I know of no cure for it; nor have I ever seen it cured before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And as for the work, when it is in the bone or can be pulled out, as we have said, you must purge the black bile from the patient once; then make it whole if it shows any swelling; then drain the patient; that is, give him good liquid to make the work; then extract your nails or the tumor, and the head of all parts, and the bone of all parts, without leaving anything in place; and leave the wound open, and press your hand or anything else firmly against it, and if the blood flows from the artery or vein, do not cauterize it too much lest it be stained; then cure it with other remedies until it is healed.

Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	From ydropisie.
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Believe the patient right on your hands, and the minister presses the belly downwards towards the lowest part of the gut, then take the hook spicule as follows: And let it be trenchant from two and a half inches to the point, and do not make it so wide that it can pass into the intestine when you insert it, and do not make it slippery;
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	Then look if the dropsy is confined to the intestines: if it is likely that you will make incisions two fingers’ breadth to the right of the navel; and if the dropsy is caused by liver disease, make your incision to the left of the navel two fingers’ breadth; and if it is caused by bile, make it to the right, and do not let the patient rest on the incision except for the fluid which escapes from that weak limb.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	Then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and the gut, and keep your hand over the entire area between the skin and the bladder as if you were escorting the amount of a nail or as thick as an entorse; then pierce the bladder until the area of the area comes out, and that is the source of the pain, then draw out the instrument, and this is the form of the instrument: it is like a silver needle, and is made of hemp or flaxseed, and has at the top a small perforation; or costs as much as half a penny, that is, two perforations; and three on one side, and one on the other. The head of the instrument is cut off like a pen, and that is the form of the incision which the writer makes like a pen
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	Then comes the ailment, if when the instrument comes into the water, if now you put your hand on the instrument; empty out half or a third of the urine, for if you empty more than that at this hour, by chance the patient will die from the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he will vomit, or he will approach death.
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	But according to the amount of its virtue, and according to what the arrangements of the virtue tell the patient and his pulse, then take the instrument and hold the water, for it is retained now by the thumb which is stamping the part which is above the facet, as I have said; pierce according to this method. Then repeat the instrument on the other side, if you see the patient suffering from this, and take up a small amount of water.
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. de l’estopement de la verge	of the belly of the limb.
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Never are children born without a navel, or if they are, their navel is small or not in its place. If the physician suspects that the navel has not pierced at all, or is too little, or is not in its rightful position: then let him cause the navel to pierce by a subtle instrument, and bind and hold it for two or three days. And when he has seen that he can urinate without pain, if he restrains the closing, he will urinate and then release it; for in this way it will not close again, for the urine that comes out forces it open.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	If the navel is too little, if it is treated with a clamp of lead, as we have said, and it swells up. Those who do not have the navel in their place are pale, for no one is born with the navel at the top of the belly, for they cannot urinate before they lift up their belly; and they cannot urinate backwards because the matter cannot come down to the marrow, and this is an evil sickness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the way of the work is that if the patient lies supine on his back, then stretch out the head of the shoulder and the arm as wide as a pen, if the navel is pierced in the middle, as it should be; and hold back the discharge of blood that comes many times, and if it comes, if the stain of this blood is seen, cure the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	Des pustules de la verge.
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these boils appear on the verge, and are a sign of foul matter; and there are both malignant and benign ones. If you wish to remove them, you must first apply a subtle ointment, then lance and crush them all, then apply a soaked cotton swab in Egyptian order; then bind with a diafinicon until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. And if the boil is malignant, with black colour and discharging, if you wish to remove it, you must apply cautery. When you have lanced it, and if the boil is at the end of the verge and has part in the skin and part outside, if you wish to close the boil which is inside first; and when it is healed, if you cure the outside. For when you cure everything together, if you do not secure the shoulder of the verge that it is not pierced, there comes blackness and corruption in the verge and elsewhere; if you wish to avoid this, remove everything that is black and corrupted, then apply honey and flour made from pomegranate peel and sometimes, then cure with other cures until it is healed.</start_of_turn
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	If blood flows freely, if the lunar cautery is used as directed in this fashion: When blood flows freely, and the limb is corrupted; and if the head of the bone is corrupted and drawn back, if you drink or pass urine a fistful of lead, and urinate on the patient among other things; and when the hair has grown over the root of the bone which has not been circumcised, or if there is a wound or incision, then you must burn with the cautery over the instrument until the ligament is loosened and the bone is freed from all parts.
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	If this is a grievous matter, if you burn over the instrument without touching the head of the bone or the skin; then open widely between the joints and put in a soft bandage of wet linen on the cold water, so that it does not slip out of place.
de la circoncision	from the circumcision.
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not merely a continuation of other wounds; although when we make this work of our own free will, and do it properly, if we make it better, it is the lightest in health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the old ones did not speak of circumcision in their laws, because they did not use it in their customs, and we have only what we have learned through experience
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the greatest part of masters and physicians who made circumcision around here, with force and all their skill; but when the urine escaped through the pores because there were two holes, and by chance if we cut off these above and left those below, the patient fled.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or la recovient coper, and the pain is doubled, and at the movement which is done too roughly, the point of the limb is not securely held; and by the movement of the bone by chance escapes the needle, and repairs the work, and many times they are born again without having had to move them and I desire it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the movement which is made there is force throughout the whole thread that I have proved to be beneficial in the experiment, for the forces tear just as well from above as from below.</start_of_turn>
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	For when you press your hand, if you make it even in every way; but if the thread is well twisted around the leather; and if the manner of the first work makes the child think, if he understands, that you do not force him to bind the thread around the limb too tightly, but that you make him enjoy it in all the ways that you can.</start_of_turn
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	Then grasp your hands straight out, and restore the forces between your hands or withdraw your fingers so that the fetus does not see them, not any of the instruments; then bring your hand to the navel and breathe or cough, and pull up as much as the head of the fetus is ensnared; then thoroughly cleanse the area that is assembled, then tie the cord with a double thread, then tie it again with another thread; and hold the two ends of the second thread to the pouch and the index finger, and cross between the two threads, then keep the thumb relaxed and pull out the head of the umbilical cord.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then let the blood flow freely without pressure, for that is the midwives; and sprinkle on and under the sprinkle a cloth glued with a soft egg yolk broken from rosewater, confirmed with rosemary oil and balsam, and leave it on until the other side is ready, and cure it again until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The shape of the forces at the circumcision is thus: the two thumbs are tense and extended, and the fingers are as great as the thumb equally:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The pain of the mundane if it comes from the incision; therefore it is necessary that you extend your fingernail, even if the wound makes a postscript; and hold it equally, and if you do not wish to hold it at your fingernail, if you hold it with your teeth, and then hold it.</p>
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they trespass for two days, and that which is beside the bone is inflamed, if you leave it as long as the swelling subsides, and the redness is slight; if you hold it as you wish, and keep the bone from the part of the limb, it will cause neither damage nor pain.</p
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez. dou retenement de l’urine	Dou retenement de l’urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is due to obstruction of the stone, or of blood congealed, or of fat, or of hair, or of similar things, which we have mentioned in the previous part.
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	If the urine does not flow freely, and you see that the retention is due to the stone which is in the belly or the neck of the bladder, then it is necessary that the patient be bent forward on his knees; and that his feet be placed outside the back, and that his abdomen be extended from the part below his back, and that he be restrained from straining himself as much as possible; and then the neck of the bladder is to be forced out towards the expression of the stone above, so that the urine may flow freely again.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	And if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then it is necessary that you administer extraction with all the instruments which are called "siringes"; and this is the form: either of silver with a lead weight at the end like a bird’s beak; or the caine of a palm of a long and a half, or of silver.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren .i. fil double, et lie au chief .i. poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	And thus it is done with the issuing of urine if you take one and a half threads of silk, and bind one end to the chief of wool or cotton, and pass the end through the bladder; and drain the surplus of wool and pass until the end reaches the head of the bladder, then join the bladder with oil or butter and beeswax from an egg, and make the patient sit on one seat, and raise the bladder and the testicles with oil moistened and olive oil and hot water.
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then put the bladder in the vagina until it reaches the root of the vagina, and double the vagina backwards against the pelvis; then drain the bladder until it reaches the bladder, and feel the patient urinate until it reaches the empty thing, and that is not done except in this order for that which leads or goes is twisted; then cut the thread at the wool end and the end, and the urine follows the wool, then pull it out forcefully, and correct the urine.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and start the bladder again until the bladder is empty, and make the patient align himself.
des maladies de la vessie	Des maladies de la vessie.
