Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When urine or blood comes into the bladder, or when pus is assembled there, and you see urine and medicines distilled, if you do everything that is called the «clepsedre», which is its shape:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	It is closed, and if it is pierced twice: once from one side, and once from the other, as you see; and the urine flows out as soon as the medicine is applied, so that the moisture is driven out, and the bladder is emptied as much as possible.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	and when you see the medicines leaking from the bladder, put the chief of the cautery into the moisture, and draw out what is causing the infection; if you draw out the moisture from the wound, and then push it back forcefully; if the moisture enters again, and comes to the bladder, the patient will feel it.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is in this manner that the bladder is ligated with a subtle twist, as when it is thus:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a .i. sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les .ij. seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe .i. poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	It is in this manner that the bladder is ligated with a subtle twist, as when it is thus: with silver or gold, and the head is higher; and the veins are cut at the breast or at the groin. Then take a bladder from a goat and put the moisture that you see ligating the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts, form a knot with a double thread, and burn the said moisture upon the fire; then withdraw the clamp from the twist in the belly, and strain your hand over the bladder with all the moisture that comes out, until the patient feels that the said moisture has reached the bladder.
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai .i. cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute .i. fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble .i. dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	and if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce it round about; then withdraw a strong thread through these holes, and assemble the circle as if you were assembling a wheel, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie it with the instrument; and do as you would with a bladder, press your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	Of the stone.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already mentioned in the preceding parts the methods of dealing with stones, and their extraction with medicines; and we mentioned the difference between a retained stone and one that is not, and the signs of each. In what case should we perform an incision for a stone? In the bladder and the kidney; and I shall tell you openly and concisely.</start_of_turn>
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that a stone which is retained in the bladder is often the cause of vomiting, and this is a sign that the bladder is greatly irritated throughout its substance; there is open hazing, and the patient feels great pain in the belly and has many vomiting spells, and then grows pale; and from these vomiting spells the foundation is loosened; and it is light for the patient to recover from vomiting until the age of three, and is much more difficult in the elderly, and is like that in young people and old people; and the cure for the large stone is easier than for the small one.</start_of_turn
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the treatment, if it is necessary, first cleanse the patient with a clustery solution, to remove all the filth from the intestines. For it never hinders to inquire about the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then grasp the patient by the limbs, loosen and move downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and never reaches the upper part; then make him sit between your hands, and his hands should rest on his thighs, so that the bladder is completely relaxed below; then inquire and touch around there.</start_of_turn>
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the stone in the space, if you hasten to cut above the stone. And if it does not yield to the touch of the whole hand, if the patient is fat, or your middle finger, if the patient is young and robust; press downwards on your left hand, if the patient is old, or your right hand, if the patient is young and robust; and hold it firmly, and inquire about the stone, and when you feel it in your right hand, if the bladder is full at the neck; then press above your right hand, and the stone will go out either by itself or you will see it cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the testicles upwards, and with his left hand to grasp the skin covering the testicles in the part where the size is taken; then insert the speculum covering, since this is the shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And put between what is between the testicles and the foundation, do not go inside but along the left edge; and be two above the stone, and two either adjoined or on the foundation, and be the size through if it is wide from the outside, and narrow inside, according to the quantity of the stone, do not go too big;
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	By chance the press if two must be at the stone or foundation, that it will leap forward in the work; and the folds that are in the stone or that are angled, and margins: if they are grasped to be still; and if there is any part that is sweaty, similar to a gland, round, from which issue is slight.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	If there are angles or margins at this place, make the size larger; and if it does not yield, know that you must draw upon the tendons which are like a file at the head, in order to draw out the stone if it does not escape; or you may give it a blow with an instrument that is curved at the head. If you do not know how to manage it, it is better to leave the stone uninjured rather than to fracture the bones.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	If there is more than one stone, draw out the largest one from the belly button first, then go up and down, and take out the smaller ones afterwards. If it is very large, cover it with silk and make a greater wound. For indeed, these things happen to the patient: either he dies, or his urine comes out too quickly and cannot be held together; but whatever you do to try to drain it, or to remove the tendons, as long as you drain it piecemeal.
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	When you have finished your work, apply incense, aloe, and dragon's blood to the wound, and tighten it. Put upon it a moist bandage of oil and wine, or oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the burn; then raise the patient up on his heel and do not loosen the bandage until the third part of the day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you release it, if there is much swelling of the limb due to oil and water, then treat with ointment of beeswax and ointment of alum, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	If pus comes out of the wound and corrosion, and blood clots in the bladder, and whether it be that the urine is retained, which is known to be in part like this without straining with the urine: do not then retain the urine in the wound, but draw out that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and carry it away.</start_of_turn>
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	Then lift the wound of water and ease and bind it securely, and help in every way you can, until it is healed; and make sure that all the hours you treat it, that you bind the wound tightly and gather the medicines above the limb.</start_of_turn
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	And if the stone is small, and it is in a tube or passage of the kidney, and is fixed there, and the urine cannot pass; if the physician does this which I have said above, that you must loosen the stone many times, for we have seen that this is effective in this case. I have seen this already.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take hold of the iron as described above and make it so that there are two angles fixed at one end in a loop:
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	Then take one thread and tie it around the kidney stone at the base of the stone, so that it does not come back into the bladder; then hold the iron against the kidney slightly, until it reaches the stone; and twist the iron back and forth at the stone until you can pierce the stone from the other side; if the urine comes, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is in the kidney. If it breaks, and urine spurts out, and the patient is in pain;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you cannot do this for any reason, take hold of one side of the bone and the other above, then draw the limb over the bone between the two joints, and then extract it forcefully, loosen the ligament, and massage the blood clot which is in the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	If you cannot do this for any reason, take hold of one side of the bone and the other above, then draw the limb over the bone between the two joints, and then extract it forcefully, loosen the ligament, and massage the blood clot which is in the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	When the bone is loosened in women, and this does not happen often, if it happens once, the cure is grief, and is hindered by two things: the first is that the woman is a virgin; the second is that one cannot find a woman who is truly virtuous, even among the most chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third method is if by chance one cannot find a woman who is truly skilled in this work of hands; and the fourth method is if the woman's stone is more prominent than the man's, for in that case one can make a greater depth, and greater fear has it.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And if necessary, if one must take a mistress who is truly knowing, and prick her root firmly, and if you do not find one, no matter how much you seek; cast her out like an useless worm; and present a woman who is wise in life, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and command her to do what you command of her by the inquiry of the stone.
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and look well if the woman is a virgin: then you must push her breast or foundation and inquire about the stone; and if she finds it, if you constrain her stomach, and command her to hold her left hand on the bladder, and press and pull her hand.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If that be true, if you must move the bowels from their entrance at the belly downwards as far as they reach the root of the thigh; then hold the heel on the piere at the root of the thigh and find the middle of the bone, where it is usually hidden, and feel the bone in that part; and do not move it from the heel downwards or downwards, and let the size be small at first.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	Then put the heel back in place at the same size. If you feel the bone is too wide for the wound, and that many kinds of bones are like this: small and large, sharp and blunt, long and round, which have reins. If the bones resemble each other, it is an indication of discharge.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if it does not go away, if you put in place a soaked piece of vitriol, and hold it for an hour until it is dry; then return to your work, until the bone is healed, and have the instruments I told you about for extracting the bone as your companions in your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	If it does not go by itself, and it is the artery that is severed, put powder on the limb and bind tightly with thread and bandage, and do not attempt to move it again, but leave the wound alone and do not touch it, except by chance the patient dies; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	When the color of blood has subsided and the limb is relaxed, if you return to your work while the wound is still open, as long as the wound is still bleeding.
de hernie carnouse	hernia of the intestines.
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing else but an assembly of moisture or white fat, which is as soft as the kernels of corn, that contains the yolk; and it is called "syfac," and never is it properly within the yolk, if we take care that it is not otherwise. And it is the skin of the kernel between the white fat that we have said. And these do not move together.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the formation of this ramus is from weakness and comes from the kernels, and the matter is spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And never does it come from percussion on the kernels, and this moisture has many colors: or it is pale yellow, or it is without red, or black, or pale blue, and such is more;
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And these are the signs of a dislocation in this assembly, for if it is white or yellowish as we have said, if the abscesses are round like the head of an egg and do not open, because there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the very flesh, if the abscesses are round with a part of the egg, and because of this it is thought that this is another egg;
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if the moisture is between the skin of the nails and the yellowish, if one feels well; then when you see the color of the moisture, if it extends to the whole surrounding area, that is like before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, therefore, which follows the introductor, judge of that which is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	When we bandage with iron, if it is necessary, that the patient be quiet and still according to his need; then bind on his back, on something somewhat high, and put on him a coat of cloth.
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	then sit on his left side, and command the minister to sit on his right side, and extend the limb towards one of the ribs as far as the ribs will go;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the sponge soaked in the liquid, and cut the skin of the ribs among the ribs as far as the thumb will go, and be careful to tear the skin completely straight by dividing the skin of the ribs until you reach the white layer, and do so slowly according to his need;
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Then pierce the surface of the abscess with a large opening, drain all the pus, and then put on your gloves; extend the abscess upwards; and do not touch the core of the abscess, but only the surrounding area; cut through all or in pieces the cost of its substance, for if you do not cut it thoroughly, the pus will return.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the upper part of the abscess has burst forth from your work, if you leave it in its place when you have finished the work of the abscess; then join together again the parts of the core of the abscess at a costure, and cure it as with other wounds, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the abscess corrupted by another disease, then you must tie up the blood vessels that are suspended, doubting the decay of blood; then cut through the abscess thoroughly, drain the pus, and cure it as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	If it is put together with its other half, and there are two roots which make up these two parts; if you have made the other part even like the first, then dry the blood, and put into the wound a cloth soaked in rose oil.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	put on another cloth soaked in wine and oil, and put on the two bones, and put on doubled cloths, and bind it up in the fashion which is proper for this form:
Puis pren .ij. drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les .ij. angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	Then take two cloths, and use coarse wool like this in the semblance and join them together at the armpits, and one of the arms grasps on the foundation up to the shoulder, and the other to the part below the shoulder; and the other two fingers grasp the two angles, and all be assembled so that the restriction is in the loop of the arm.
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	And never is this cautery branch useful for the size of iron; take only a superficial cautery, and burn the skin of the joint, and if it be eschaufed as we have said, so that the white substance which contains the pain is discovered.
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	If you take the cautery as we have said, and pierce this membrane as we have shown, and burn with this superficial cautery,
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	And keep doing it in all ways that you can, until you have burned through everything; and keep the fire away from the flesh; and be careful that this matter is more salve; and do not remove blood, and do not make haste in the work.
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	If nothing else hinders you, or if a vein bursts or blood vessel bursts or any other thing, if you can, remedy what hinders you, according to what is said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai,	If the patient is faint and cannot endure this work because of its horror, if you perceive an opening, as I have said, and if you are quite certain from the signs we have mentioned that the wound is fluid-filled,
si fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege leveit; puis perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	If you make the patient sit up; then pierce the abscess at the lower part with all the surrounding tissue wide open, and pierce the hole through the bone; and if the wound is large, so that all the pain is expelled immediately
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	Then put cotton on the limb and bind it, and let the remaining pain run its course; then cure it until the wound is healed.
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge .i. poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés .vj. mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	If the white cloth does not stop the pain at the wound's source, if you should drink a penny or the instrument used for treating the hydropic wound, as it is formed in this way; and make it wide. That is, enlarge the wound, and drain that the pain may return, and reassemble after about twenty days or until it heals, and when it is reassembled as before, the patient will then be well again.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the excision of the testicles.
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Hair that is in this section of the limb has doubt and fear in many places, for I think that it is worth leaving it as it is.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	I will tell you about the work and the signs of the incision
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Therefore, when the abscess comes or bursts, and there are stitches; and this is often the case
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It is known by excessive swelling and pain, which is spread out as stitches, or by percussion;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	And it is the color of the abscess according to the color of the urine; and there is no pain, and it is an abscess of grief.
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	And sometimes an abscess is grieved with fear and pain, and is of a dark color, and never comes from a vein or swelling of a vessel.</start_of_turn>
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is not from a vein, if it is known by the disposition of the cautery abscess, when you press it at your side;
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and you must not touch it.</start_of_turn>
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	He who makes an engorgement of a vein is known by his disposition at the expression of touch of the two thumbs.
et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	and can well make the size of this semblance, and on the other limbs
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and that you clip the nerves like nails, then the yolk is up, and the thread from the white sack comes out, and release the suspension from all parts of the yolk.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the yolk is already clotted with these nails, if you must then treat the yolk, and clip it.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	And if it is towards the socket, or within the blood vessels, if you must deliver all that is tense, and round off the edges.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if it is towards the socket, or within the blood vessels, if you must deliver all that is tense, and round off the edges.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is done, if you apply a bandage of coarse wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then cure with other cures until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a .i. borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions,	This is an abscess enclosed by a covering similar to a berry, with softening of the bones.
et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	The patient groans in pain when he moves it
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant,	and the treatment for this disease is very painful as well as this one before
et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	And all these things we will tell you about in the following chapters, according to what the ancients have made.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois,	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on the edge of the bed, and then hold the supporter of the collarbones above his shoulders.
a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	Hold all the ribs that protrude at the waist, and keep them stretched out, and hold the master steady and extend them forward;
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert,	then grasp the scapula wide and uncover the blood vessels until they are fully exposed,
et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	and then support the shoulder blade from below, as we have mentioned in the extraction of arteries from the temples;
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	Then I insert a needle or if there is a double thread, I tie it to the first root or where the nail has come out, and I tie it to the other root.
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	Then I press them [the roots] together firmly, according to the length of the hair, and I extract the corrupted moisture.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	Then I treat the wound like the others or I bandage it, so that no blood vessel is torn except for those which nourish the surrounding parts;
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	for in this way there is no harm, and if all the blood vessels are torn, if you must, you can pull out the bones from all the blood vessels.
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	If the oes does not lose its nourishment through the incision of the vessels, and dries and does not yield aid.
de la routure dou syfac	If the oes does not lose its nourishment through the incision of the vessels, and dries and does not yield aid.
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	If the oes does not lose its nourishment through the incision of the vessels, and dries and does not yield aid
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces .ij. manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	If the oes does not lose its nourishment through the incision of the vessels, and dries and does not yield aid.
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	And the signs when it is an extension of the jaw, if there is much swelling and much tension, long and sustained, and does not come immediately;
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	And the swelling is equal on both sides up to the earlobe, because the jaw presses the intestine.</start_of_turn>
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the sign is when the jaw is fractured, that it suddenly causes pain in the ear, and the swelling is different from the normal, with the skin taut and pale, because of the escape of the intestine and the swelling of the jaw.</start_of_turn
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never do the bones move with the intestine, and is retained when forced, and causes great suffering to the patient, even when pressed.</start_of_turn>
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these fiery cures with fear, for fear itself suffices.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And if you command or patient that he grasp the intestines with his hand in the wound, if he can reinsert them there;
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then either hold his neck between your hands, and grasp his genitals;
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then extend the arm at the shoulder, and strip all the hair along the groin;
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	Then from the depth of the wound, take the leathers of the size of uncorns according to what you must master to open the wound, and be such that they can be easily removed.
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	Then pull out the fat that is under the leather of the wound, until the white fat of the marrow is discovered throughout;
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac,	Then put your thumb inside the wound where the marrow bone is, between the white fat that is under the outer skin and the second fat layer,
et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	and pull out what is behind the marrow, and between the second fat layer; and hold the thumb of your right hand inside the wound, and extend the white fat upwards with your left hand, and keep the marrow bone towards the size of the wound.
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	And command the minister to extend the arm upwards, and loosen what is behind the limb.
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	And ask at the same time if there is any intestine or white fat wrapped around the limb, and if you find nothing, if it is in the belly below
puis pren une aguille ou il ait .i. gros fil fait de .x. filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait .iiij. filz;	Then take a needle or if there is any thick thread made of thread, and insert it into the back part of the fat, which is after the skin of the buttocks; after that, the size, then cut the nails that appear from the thread, until there are three threads left;
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de .ij. pars;	Then assemble the one over the other in the manner of a cross, and bind the fat, which we have said is the skin of the buttocks, with a strong thread of.ij. parts.
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de .ij. pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	Then cover the head of the shoulder with cloth, and bind it firmly with .ij. parts, so that no vessel except those that nourish it can enter there, only at the incision it must remain.
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc .ij. dois de celui, et aprés ces .ij. liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	Then straighten the limb according to the first limb that is long .ij. two of them, and after these .ij. limbs leave out the fat which is as soft as the kernels of corn at the greatest heat of a pot of lentils
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	and after that the rest according to the curve that the egg carries; then press in the part which is as soft as the leather of the nails, as much as it will stay put, and bend, as we have said above.
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	Then apply soft wool soaked in oil to the wound, and put on a dressing, and I will tell you what to do.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	Never cauterize the flesh except as I have said after the incision, in doubt of bloodletting
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	For this often happens, and leave the limb until it bleeds by itself; and if it bleeds too slowly, if it happens that the wound has become infected with hot water, and put on what I have said, until it bleeds.
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Then cure the wound with another dressing, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	De hernie carnouse.
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this limb I have never seen anyone who could cure it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the old folks say that it is made just like the limb which is bound to the screw, in part like when you bind the blood vessels, after the size above lightly at the bottom;
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put some salve on it, and cure the abscess of what it causes; as long as the blood vessels bite; and cure it as we have said, as long as it is healthy.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	Never comes routine with anger, as we have said, and open the veins; and do not leave any intestines inside, for if there are any, that is enough, and repair them at all hours.
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and if it stays too long in this place, if one believes the wound or tumor, as long as the intestines are leaving;
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this comes from the swelling of the flesh which is angry, as we have said, because it is stretched, then it is softened and relaxed, and opens the veins
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and it is cured by cautery, as we have previously said; and never by iron in this manner:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	And it is that the patient lies prone upon his back between your hands, then seize the limb of the affected area with a large clamp according to the quantity of two thumbs.
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	And then draw out the scab which is below the skin that covers it, then take hold of the root and pull out the limb that appears from the scab.
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	And press at the navel, then cut the two thumbs that appear from the scab on the top of the root, and cut one and the other;
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	Then draw out the root, and do not cover the scab or extend the belly or anything else, as I told you in the treatment of the hernia of the intestines.
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then cure by the treatment of wounds. And when you have closed the wound, if the moisture and cure the wound, as long as it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The swelling is constrained, and has no apparent cause in the course of treatment, and the cautery is mute in this limb, and more proximate to safety.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the nails
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the nails becomes soft in old age, because the nails themselves are softened, and it is seen; and it is necessary, when it is seen to be cured, to make the patient lie on his back, and to remove the soft skin from the natural skin; then join the two layers together with a suture, and if you see that, leave the excess of soft skin at two or three sutures; then close between the sutures, and cure as with the other wounds, until it is healed, and cut the thread.
dou chastrement	Dou chastrement,
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Because of the chastament,
des hermofrodites	of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hermofrodie est selonc deux manieres: une si est que entre les deux coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine. Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et deux coions. Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.
de la tentigene	Hermaphroditism is in two ways: one if between the two testicles is open as in the figure of nature in a woman, or if there is hair, and sometimes in the urine is held back. And the other way if in women, and has on the navel as a beard and two testicles. And the cure for the swelling and fame is if you crush the testicles completely, and the cure is like for other wounds; in the second way, of men whose urine spurts through the skin of the testicles, if there is no cure.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Tentigene is a swelling that appears on the natural part [of the body], as long as it is too heavy to see; and many women have it just as much as a hand. And the cure is like that of a hand. It is necessary to keep the excess of the swelling down by your hand or as one would with a bandage; and do not press too much, for blood will not come, and then the cure will be of no use; and another disease that comes from the mouth of the marrow, and the spleen, and by chance spurts out, and is like the figure of a cow, and for this reason it is called the ancient "madness of the cows". If you can keep it down, as we have said, and the cure will be when it is healed.
de erratique	De erratique.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	When something is out of its proper place.
des emorroides	From boils.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Emorroids are openings of veins which without support are usually not cured; and when they are old they become thick; and we have already mentioned in the division the signs and symptoms, and I will say here those which bring about healing. I say that emorroids and thick blood, when they are mixed in the marrow and are not perceived, can only be cured by iron. Those which are at the mouth of the marrow can be perceived, and can be cured. It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then strengthen the ankle and hold the shin bone in its roots, then sprinkle upon it medicinal astringents such as acacia and dragon’s blood and incense, and similar things; then close the wound an hour later, then bathe it in cold water; and if there is any remaining blood, if she sits in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and barley and similar things, and then drink barley flour, and mix it with honey and oatmeal, and make one application on her back. And if it stops bleeding, that is good. If not, if there is still bleeding, make her breathe with a cloth over her back and apply pressure; then take linen, and moisten it with the juice of plantain or the juice of elderberry with wine vinegar, and make her breathe. And when the wound has healed, if it is not completely cured, it will become white like a rough chief; if you cover it as I have said the thick blood. And then it will be cured when it is completely healed.
des apostemes de la marris	Emoroids are openings of veins which without support are usually not cured; and when they are old they become thick; and we have already mentioned in the division the signs and symptoms, and I will say here those which bring about healing. I say that emorroids and thick blood, when they are mixed in the marrow and are not perceived, can only be cured by iron. Those which are at the mouth of the marrow can be perceived, and can be cured. It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then strengthen the ankle and hold the shin bone in its roots, then sprinkle upon it medicinal astringents such as acacia and dragon’s blood and incense, and similar things; then close the wound an hour later, then bathe it in cold water; and if there is any remaining blood, if she sits in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and barley and similar things, and then drink barley flour, and mix it with honey and oatmeal, and make one application on her back. And if it stops bleeding, that is good. If not, if there is still bleeding, make her breathe with a cloth over her back and apply pressure; then take linen, and moisten it with the juice of plantain or the juice of elderberry with wine vinegar, and make her breathe. And when the wound has healed, if it is not completely cured, it will become white like a rough chief; if you cover it as I have said the thick blood. And then it will be cured when it is completely healed.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	Emoroids are openings of veins which without support are usually not cured; and when they are old they become thick; and we have already mentioned in the division the signs and symptoms, and I will say here those which bring about healing. I say that emorroids and thick blood, when they are mixed in the marrow and are not perceived, can only be cured by iron. Those which are at the mouth of the marrow can be perceived, and can be cured. It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then strengthen the ankle and hold the shin bone in its roots, then sprinkle upon it medicinal astringents such as acacia and dragon’s blood and incense, and similar things; then close the wound an hour later, then bathe it in cold water; and if there is any remaining blood, if she sits in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and barley and similar things, and then drink barley flour, and mix it with honey and oatmeal, and make one application on her back. And if it stops bleeding, that is good. If not, if there is still bleeding, make her breathe with a cloth over her back and apply pressure; then take linen, and moisten it with the juice of plantain or the juice of elderberry with wine vinegar, and make her breathe. And when the wound has healed, if it is not completely cured, it will become white like a rough chief; if you cover it as I have said the thick blood. And then it will be cured when it is completely healed.
de l’enfantement	From infancy
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	From infancy, the midwife first perceives the natural figure of an infant when she sees the woman press down on the navel and desire to smell the afterbirth; then the child immediately comes out; so that when the child is born according to the natural figure, the head comes out first, and the second hand follows; and when you see these signs, if you gently press on the abdomen, the child will come out headfirst; for when it descends on the head, the second hand follows, and the mother is saved from the burden of her afterbirth by the bones of the body; and this is not natural. For it never comes from its joints, but from force of the womb or the child, or the hands, or it comes from the abdomen or the navel, and is converted by an accident from its collar, and by other harmful figures; if the midwife is skilled in the art, she will be wary of errors and deceptions, and I will show you all the figures that we must use to aid her.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	When the child comes out naturally from the head and the woman gives birth and the strength of the child is weak, if you make her sit on a stool, or the women hold her; and when she has relaxed with oil or rue or fennel, which is customary, then you should hold the child between your two arms and gently push the little heel that gives it its shape:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And cut the second [bone], and hold its nail until the moisture that is within corrects itself; and seize the woman’s belly until the fetus descends, and if it does not descend, if you must, clench the woman with muscle from fennel seeds with olive oil; then make her gulp and cough up phlegm, and keep her mouth and nose closed for an hour: if the fetus is now out. And if the thumbs come out too far, if you must, keep them lightly flexed back and forward; and if they will not enter, put the woman on her side, and hold her feet high; then withdraw the seat from the earth, and hold her, that she does not cough; and if the thumbs do not enter, and the fetus is dead, if you must, clench the thumbs at the wrist which is above, and pull out the fetus, and raise her equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	From the issue of the child from its feet.
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child comes from its feet, if you can push upwards;
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	And then the shoulder joint will pop forward and backward, until it is even.
puis preigne .i. des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	and then take hold of the limb and extend it forward and backward.</start_of_turn>
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	until it is even.
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If the limb leaps up again, God help us.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not forced as we have said, if the joint hangs too low or too high, as long as it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For in such a case it is easily displaced.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	And if it is not forced as we have said, if take muscle from above, and oil of lint, and gum masticated, and grind all this together in a mortar;  </start_of_turn
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement,	and put on the nature of the woman inside and drive away this swelling.</start_of_turn>
puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	Then let him sit upright in water up to his ribs;
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai .i. coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	And when it is moist, let him drink a spoonful of myrrh and give him wine, and leave him for an hour.
puis la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	Then let him sit on a chair, then make him spit and strain his mouth and throat, and gently palpate his belly, for he will now jump up.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	because of the child’s discharge from his genitals.
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the boy comes in this shape, if he puts his hands on his face and on his head;
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor .i. lit;	then either he sniffs his collar and hangs his tongue out, or he blows his nose with his fists.</start_of_turn>
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	he folds his hands on his chest and then takes his hands and grasps his stomach, pressing on the belly button until it is visible again.</start_of_turn
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	if the boy does not cough, then take his hands and move his feet, then move his stomach up and down, and then take back your hands;
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	And thus the boy sobs and sobs; and instructs the woman to take care of him until the boy is well.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	and the boy cries out loud; and instructs the woman to look after him until the boy is well.
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	I must order you to restore the limb:
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if it cannot be restored, if you must leave the woman, and call for help;
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus .i. lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	If it does not move, if you manage to grasp it by the lit, and it lets go of the legs,
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then support the limb as I have described;
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if it still does not budge, if you manage to hold it in its seat, then study how to remove the limb;
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and gently pull it out in its natural position, and make it spit, and command it to remain stretched out until it is relieved.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	From the issue of the child on his neck, and his hands spread out, and his face turned towards his mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	I believe that the boy is holding out his hand, then turning it back and forth, and pressing it lightly;
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	When it is even, if you put on the muscular substance of altitude and oil, as we have said, then command that it moves back and forth.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	When you have done this, if you make it sit on its seat, and command it to bend; and it will sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	From this same manner at all the second time.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes forcefully in this manner at all the second time, if the second time reaches your nail, as long as moisture is evacuated;
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and if the nail is bent over its face and its collar, if the head of the bone is loosened, that it does not remain, and the patient dies.
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then withdraw the child, as long as you have put it as it should be, and command the woman not to move at all:
adonques si istra legierement.	When it is gently pulled.
de l’issue des gemelz	Then if it is easily pulled out
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Then if it is easily pulled out, the nails which grow often do not grow at the same time; and this is not a strange thing, and often happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two are strange things, and do not live long, if only for that name.
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know well that they are numerous, and they are loosened by the substance which devours them, which is bound to the bud.
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	and never depart so naturally as all at once, as we have said before.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if it departs cruelly, if the cure is as we have said, and be it a subtle seizure, and make haste and lightly do what it does;
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and do so as it is worth doing for health.
de plusors enfans	Moreover.
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	Moreover, sometimes they are formed in masses, that is to say in groups of one, two, three, four, five, six, or seven, or more up to fifteen, and are all formed in the shape of a child by the measure of their glorious stature.
et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	and it is necessary that she should dance all this, for by chance many things happen;
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	if you do it as it should be done.
de l’enfant mort	Of dead children.
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you cure the woman of a dead child or unborn child, as I have said in the division, and there is no immediate relief, and you are compelled by the work of your hands;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	you must believe that the woman is of sound mind and has no accident or fear of death.
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	if you believe that the woman is conscious on her back, and her limbs are inclined downwards, and her legs are lifted;
et li ministre la teigne de .ij. pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	And if the handmaid grasps her wrist with fifteen fingers, or if she is bound to the bed if she does not descend from the child;
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	Then wipe the mouth of the basin with moist oil, mixed with alum and fenugreek seeds and linseed oil, and anoint her hands with these oils and these mixtures.
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere .i. leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu,	Then place her in the basin lightly, and give her one or two leeches that are convenient for this purpose,
et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	Take care that the child is not left hanging over his head.
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez,	If the hair in the armpits, or in the neck, or in the mouth, or on the face, or on the beard, or in the hair of the eyebrows, or on the eyelashes, or on the cheeks,
et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	and if they detach downwards on the face, it is grasped or plucked out, and the eyebrows droop down.
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and you must hold the hair with your right hand, and place the thumb between the two of your left hand, and grasp with all your hand lightly, and hold the hair in none of these ways that we have said, until it comes to the empty thing;
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and that is the form of the hair:
puis fiche encontre .i. autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	Then the limb finds another support, or the third party intervenes, if so the extraction must be even.
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then it extends equally by moving from side to side, because of moisture, and the nails of the fingers are loosened by moisture, or the teeth of the bones are loosened by moisture which must be held, as in this case:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if it remains in part, if once the limb has been bailed with oil around its circumference, and the nails of the fingers are bound in that part, and the other part is treated;
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if there remains no part, if you put this ointment or higher up inside, and do so until it has gone away entirely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement,	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be pulled back by stretching,
si covient que tu envoloupes sus .i. drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	then you must wrap around the drapeil until it is whole.</start_of_turn>
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as .ij. piés.	then hold it at the joint of the limb or at the root, and ensure that you do the same with the other hand, and have two thumbs.</start_of_turn>
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee,	and if the shoulder joint is large and is twisted in the extraction, or if there is pain in the assembly,
si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	If it be certain that you have pushed back the bony prominence between your two hands, and have fixed the head, then draw out the pain.
