ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	or you shall bind it to the instrument which is called the «almidach», from which it forms along with the instruments or bandage which follows this;
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and thus make it swell naturally with great force;
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles,	and then treat for the bones as tenacious,
et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	If the shoulder joint is forced out by force and is strained by the forcele, if it is fractured, as long as the moisture which is either coming out or has come out.
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	if it cannot be restored, if the bone breaks into pieces at the muscle that you put in place;
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	if it is swollen in the belly or deforms the ribs, if you must pierce through as much as the moisture goes out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	if it is above its pieces, if the attraction is slight, and the receiving end of the tube is lighter.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a .i. drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is twisted in the belly or the wrist, it is necessary to draw it out, that is, to uncover it that is covering the hand.
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and hold the belly or the wrist, until the moisture that is causing the pain is expelled.
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure,	and if another part is fractured and the limb is immobile,
si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	if the limb is pierced by an iron or the like, from the armpit to the wrist;
puis i boute .i. oncine ou ij., et le trai fuer;	Then I command thee. I anoint thee or I join thee, and I force the evil away.
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier,	and if there is moisture in the mouth, it is pushed back by the cautery which has come, if I cannot bear it,
ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	then I must bring moist and oily things.
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and I mix plaster, and soak it in soft and moist water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the fetus is on its side, put it even, if necessary reminding what was said about the living child.
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and if it does not move, if it is forced out by pieces, and you leave nothing of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, if necessary remind what was said about the afterbirth that comes with the mare;
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if blood comes out, if there is any other cure.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman who had a child in her womb that was dead, then consulted with another about it, and refuted death for the other.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, there came a swelling in the belly that opened, and caused great pain
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I went for help, and for a long time I thought, and could not stop the pain.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a strong plaster, and out came a bone, and after a while another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marvel at your mouth, for your belly has no bone.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	I want the wound, and with hands of bone, as long as the woman is better;
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and I saw the woman long tense in pain, and that was already a little bow of blood in the body.
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	And I have never seen this chapter except for the time when the master found a strange thing, and he had to give aid.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to reset the dislocation to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	And thus comes the form of the pressor, as we must do in the books; and two returns are made for two limbs.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	However, the horn should be more subtle than the restraint, and be made of ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	And let the lips be wide open, like a large mouth, and the chin be drawn in, and the tongue be long half a palm.
et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	And between them let the two lips be closed with a gentle pressure from the middle of the face, which should be held together, half a palm or more in length.</start_of_turn>
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	And these two pressures are placed in the mouth of the patient when the two corners are opened.</start_of_turn>
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, more subtle and lighter, can be made of ebony or boxwood, according to the shape of the nails.</start_of_turn
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	And he has thus two joints of the shoulder, as you see, of a palm of length, and two of width;

Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never is copper or silver cautery made, or of wasp or molten iron; and never are these small and great instruments made as they are brought.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those who are feeble and painful in their upbringing and in their treatment are petty.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of a small and great blister is thus when it is surrounded by a wide area, or when the belly is bound in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and if there is a swelling or the belly is bound, as you see, and the head or the foot is pierced; and there is a wound at one of the sides, or from the other side.
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	or if the belly is bound with a bladder of horsehair or parchment, or if it is pierced all around the wound
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	And has between each hole [of the dressing] one must put space, then pass through these holes one strong thread of strong thread twisted in a cross or in a knot, and assemble the belly as though it were a spoke.
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And when the medicine is inside, if the thread has in front of it a strong thread, then clip it; and this is the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clip with oil or balm of egg, or something similar, and then bind it lightly;
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	Then the minister grasps his thumbs together, as long as he is whole, and pulls out the clot, and the patient extends his legs at the surface.
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And if the physician sees that it is necessary, if the wound is large; and if he sleeps all night whole, that is a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cauterize it in a state of sickness of swelling of the belly, and the physician hasten to leave, if it starts again as long as it is sane.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if there are swellings or foundations, or abscesses, if the clot is as subtle as for a child;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And thus it is with the form of a subtle blister on the skin that the leather is strained:
des plaies	And thus it is with the form of a subtle blister on the skin that the leather is strained: from wounds.
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said in the preceding section the treatment of wounds; or rather the treatment of hands and medicine, as it is completed.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are various according to the way they are made, and according to the place or the wound is made, and of what material it is made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things that cause wounds are done by the bite of stone, or the size of spear and nail, or of lance or fist or sickle, or similar things.
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or that are made according to the hardness of the flesh, as when there is a wound that pierces the neck, or the head, or the hand, or the belly, or the liver, and similar parts.
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the cure for simple wounds, and I will begin with wounds of the head, because the memory will come back to you in this chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes or a wound of the head, and the bone is not broken, if you take care that it is from the bite of stone or from similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large,
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	And you doubt with reason about incisions: if you do them too soon after an injury, it may bring about more blood than from the wound itself; or let the blood flow in the opposite direction to the affected part.
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and listen carefully to the patient’s complaints of vomiting and loss of appetite.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	If he does not recover, if he has lost his appetite for meat and does not drink wine, does not eat bread;
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and remove the wound, if there is swelling, apply a wet compress of rose oil only, or in astringent wine.</start_of_turn>
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	If there is no oozing from the wound, if you place a swab on it while it is fresh with all its blood, and it does not move by air, dust, or anything else, I will tell you later.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is any movement, place some sponges on it until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is great as if made by a sword and similar things, and the edges do not come together by tension, if you join them with sutures, as I will say, for wounds of the belly, with sutures.</start_of_turn>
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is exposed by bone, it is wide open and will only hold together by a single thread; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore flesh in place of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	Instruct the patient to consume large amounts of broth, such as broth and oatmeal, as well as poultry and other things like that.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	If you find pus or decay under the skin, but there is no bone exposed, if you grasp it firmly and pull it out, then cure it; then.</start_of_turn
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	If there is an artery or vein in the wound that cannot be staunched by medicine, if you see the artery and you can dislocate it, grasp it with a thread; </start_of_turn
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	If this does not help, if the cautery fails,
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	If these wounds are small and simple, if it is a mild cure: and if you put on this powder that adheres as soon as it moves.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	The manner of the powder is: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; chalk that burns three parts, and mix the powder thoroughly.
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and apply the wound, and hold it firm, until it is well aired and reunited with all its blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Then hold it firmly, and leave it loose, if it does not swell; for we do not bandage the medicine until it is whole.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	Never do we make this burn only, when we do not have incense or dragon’s blood, but that the wound has not moved.</start_of_turn>
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	If the wound has moved even a little, do not put anything else on it.</start_of_turn>
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but put on some digestive herbs or poultices made of oatmeal and honey, until it has sweated blood.</start_of_turn
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the treatment for other ailments as long as he is conscious.

de la plaie dou col	of the neck wound.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	Wound comes from the collar and it is simple, if there is no difference between the neck and the chest, but if the neck or the artery is severed.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If the neck is severed, if there is no other cause except to leave the wound open, and do not put anything restrictive, because it is night and it makes the neck withdraw;
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	do not put anything cold on the wound, because the substance of the neck is cold, and the continuation of the pain is with the brain, which is the most tender limb.

de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	Of wound from spear or knife.

puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then pull and strain the black blood out of your hand from the one hand to the other, as much as the patient can suffer;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	And then bind it, and command that he hold flesh around the black vein;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	And resume the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, and do no harm to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	Then the limb must be restored to its proper position: if there is any hair remaining on the patient,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then stretch out the limb, wash it, and if there is swelling in the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if there is no bath available, if you put the limb in the fire and then cool it down by applying pressure to the vein at the armpit or at the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	Then open the skin at the navel, and support the belly from under, until it opens when you feel it;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and you will see red and black, and when it enters or the skin seems like a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then stretch the wound downwards until it is level with the skin, and then close it at the navel gently,
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then cover it with another layer of skin inside and outside; and support the belly until it opens again,
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then the limb should be raised, as you have done, and the pain should be repeated on another side, as you did first.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	Then take a larger size, or several if you need to, and then raise the limb, and take hold of the limb at the shoulder blade
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then stretch and raise the limb until the second size; then pull out the limb piece by piece until it is completely straight, then grasp it
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you do not pull and raise it, if there is a strong double thread there,
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	And the shoulder and the arm, and there are some who say, right, stretch out your hand from one side and the other, until it is finished.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	And keep that it does not slip, for if it slips, it cannot be treated or lifted, and comes to harm the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have treated it, if you put out the limb of the wound with soaked wool in wine and rosemary oil; and cure it until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the limb is contracted and tortuous and bound together, and it is not right, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	If you think it is necessary to force it, do not cover it up; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron from which the pin is covered is crooked, do not burn it, but only cover the vein;

De la voinne civile	From the civil vein.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is engorged in the leg, in hot regions where herbs or trees do not grow, and in the earth where there is no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and sometimes it happens elsewhere in the leg, and this comes from the decay that comes from the softening of the leather
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	if it comes from the entrails of the serpent and towards, swell between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	and if there is a great swelling in the leg when this vein swells,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	Then the limb becomes stiff, and the vein becomes taut as a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated, if you suspect that the shoulder is dislocated, cover it with a piece of lead from one and a half inches to two inches thick, and hold the limb still,
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	until the swelling has subsided.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, if you cut off a part of it, and cover the rest, and do not cover it in its root, until it is all gone.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	For if you grasp it firmly, if it returns to the socket, make an incision and extract or retain the foreign body; and make the wound worse.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	Therefore it is necessary that it be treated promptly and thoroughly, and that nothing be left behind or remain fixed there.

Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	From veins that arise between skin and bone
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This ailment is called in our land "beef disease", forasmuch as it often occurs with boils.
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	it is a small swelling that arises between skin and bone, and spreads throughout the body, ascending and descending
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and causes the skin to wrinkle or burst, and sometimes bursts through the skin or the bone itself
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	it is accompanied by the discharge of various humors, such as blood, bile, serum, and worms or abscesses.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	And doubt arises of its wickedness, for when it goes through the flesh, and it ascends to the head, and it comes to the oil,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	And thus it returns by chance, and destroys the oil; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it cured and treated, if one cannot force it until it goes away:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	then you must bind the limb above and below with a strong and well-stitched ligature.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	Then hold above and support the limb, and if it is grasped by the heel in the char, and you do not find it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	Then hold above and support the limb, and if it is grasped by the heel in the char, and you do not find it, if the fire cautery is applied there until it swells;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	Then hold above and support the limb, and if it is grasped by the heel in the char, and you do not find it, if the fire cautery is applied there until it swells, and it causes greater harm if oil is added, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	Then hold above and support the limb, and if it is grasped by the heel in the char, and you do not find it, if you see it coming or close to oil, grasp the heel firmly and support the limb;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	And it is advised to use the patient with the application of solid medicines that dissolve for bad humors carried,
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and be wary of eating fatty foods.</start_of_turn>
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from windiness.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and is a pain that comes in the limbs,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	And thus, when a limb moves from one place to another; and I have seen that which I have told you of.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I went to a sick woman, and found her arm swollen in the armpit.
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and then, as time went on, I saw that her arm had become like a worm in the armpit,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	more swollen than anything, like living silver when it is cut from its root.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	The pain departs from that limb and settles in the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then afterwards it is turned wrong by the whole limb, so that it comes into the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then I heard that it twisted back towards the limb, just as I saw it
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I wondered what caused such a movement of the limb against the limb, for I had never seen such a disease in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Whatever be the case, I advise you to keep still and do not move, for pain in the limbs is often caused by movement to another part.
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I do not advise it for a woman;...
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I think that this is because women have dry skin and uncovered veins,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	because of this appears that constraint;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	And they do not appear to me in this regard for those who are pleasing, and who have moist flesh and veins that are well filled.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see this disease cured, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	if the swelling above and below has remained, and then ceases as soon as this constraint of the limb is overcome
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	burn the limb; and if you do not see it at your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	If the antidote for those who suffer from wind-sickness, as with foul pills, and oily pills, and similar things.
Des saiettes	If the antidote for those who suffer from wind-sickness, as with foul pills, and oily pills, and similar things.
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	If the antidote for those who suffer from wind-sickness, as with foul pills, and oily pills, and similar things.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	If the antidote for those who suffer from wind-sickness, as with foul pills, and oily pills, and similar things.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	And those which have three angles, and those which have tongues, and those where there are pieces.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	And those which have three angles, and those which have tongues, and those where there are pieces; or in the principal limb it breaks by shifting.
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in the brain, the shoulder, the elbow, the wrist, the thumb, the intestine, the bladder, and similar limbs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it breaks in no limb of these members, and the sign of death is shown, which I will tell you later, you will learn:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	If you suspect that the extraction of this arrow will cause more harm than good, for the body comes afterwards in various conditions.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And when this sign is absent, do not believe me, for the arrow is not withdrawn from its wound, if it is not treated, it will cure the wound.</start_of_turn>
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain when the arrow pierces the bone, and forces the fatty substance which is above the brain,

Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of the splinter when it hurts or swells, are that it is close to the left breast, and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, do not make it empty.

saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Indeed, doubt now suggests that death approaches.</start_of_turn>

And the sign of the seat that never lets go of its wound is that it leaps without prompting, the throat swells, the patient turns pale, and breathing is difficult.</start_of_turn

And if the arrow comes out into the bladder, and the urine comes out in spurts and comes out forcefully, and the patient feels great pain: the wound is mortal.</start_of_turn
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	As for the other limb, if it is made up of flesh and bone and the jaw and the shoulder and the elbow and the wrist and the hand, and the limb that is similar to these, they are all subject to many variations.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the splinter is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I have said before, for this reason you must do something else.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	When there is a splinter in the nerve or artery, which is not venomous, as I have said previously, for this reason you must do something else. There is at least one home remedy for this:

l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	One is the head dislocation, and is said on the left side of the breast, and they call it the people "neck vein."

Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see blood flowing out like the urine of a child, and it is pale and transparent, take that it is without an artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Haste then, for thus, place thy thumb upon its length, and hold thy thumb steady, for many times it has been thus.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	Hasten then, for thus hold thy thumb steady, and let it rest, and move it not; and be cautious, for fear lest thou move it while it is sound.</start_of_turn>
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if it is without stain, and thou feel pain, and the physician is not present, if the vein should burst, for the head of the shoulder retires itself; hold it still without stain.</start_of_turn
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a support of figs, and make it firm, and take one of the halves and bind it well up to the other shoulder;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If it remains without stain, that is good; but if not, if the doctor wishes, as we have said, powders that stain blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And staining does not hold in many situations because of the small size of the wound, and the power of the liquid blood.</start_of_turn>
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The blood from the vein helps to treat without head and chest, and bones below.</start_of_turn
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is made up of the balsamic and cephalic humors, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	And it is necessary for the physician to warn the patient that he must beware of the nerve that is below, and if it is not too deeply immersed, and he finds the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and he inflates and the sensation is either gone, or by chance cannot be cured;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	it often bursts open several times, and if it does not burst in some people because of its subtlety, it is necessary to know that you must remove the cause of the pain; and take hold of the nerve with your hand.</start_of_turn>
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, if the wound is deep.</start_of_turn
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The blood of the head helps, that it attracts blood without chief, and aids the eyes.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is advisable to cauterize with the olive or myrtle flame, for this is the safest of all veins, for it has neither nerves nor arteries.</start_of_turn>
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is necessary to inquire more gently this first time, and do not grieve if it fails the first time, and we repeat.</start_of_turn
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance it inflames the limbs of some people, which we cannot avoid the first time, but it does not grieve us.</start_of_turn
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of blood is as you think.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you must know about health is that blood is not only for maintaining health
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	but also for expelling diseases to come;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	or in the cephalic, fasting, and basilar veins.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	And it must be ascertained at the outset of treatment when the patient groans, sighs, and yawns after eating, when the sign of repletion appears.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	And it must be ascertained at the outset of treatment when the patient groans, sighs, and yawns after eating, when the sign of repletion appears.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The blood that is administered for diseases does not have a fixed dose, but only when necessary is of juice or nut, at all hours and in all tensions;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it must not be administered to children under thirteen years of age, nor to women who are pregnant more than four months until childbirth.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	They should not remain alive who have passed .lx. years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when anyone sees himself alive in any way, if it be known that he has defiled the intestines with a light fistula,
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	he has eaten excrement, so that the veins do not bring forth nourishing humours from the principal members
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	neither too fat, nor too lean, neither too hot nor too cold;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	And if he suffers from vomiting, pain in the belly, multiple fits of vomiting at women, childbirth, watching and guarding, and all his strength, either from the weapon or from pain;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then subtilize the humors, if they are not great, by meats and by drinks and by medicines, if you have the power to do so.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then enter or bathe, if nothing hinders you, to subtilize the blood,
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and keep warm the belly or the chest, as we have said before.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	And keep that of work, of pricking, of luxury, and of similar things.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	And be careful not to bind or restrain them, and let the patient rest higher than his hands which are to be warmed once or twice.</start_of_turn>
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	Then draw out the thread slowly, because if it is too tight or too loose, it cannot be corrected without.</start_of_turn
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	Then rub the limb with your hands, until the veins swell up, and you feel them.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	Then moisten the wound with a little oil, and put the thumb of your left hand on that vein below where you saw the wound, until you see the patient recover.
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	Then the vein is not firm and liable to be cut.</start_of_turn>
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins which flee just like strings to the patient, and if there are some which are filled with windiness,
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	if when you put on the flame, if you take away the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is this;
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	If he grasps the vein too tightly, if the wound is too wide, for this reason it is necessary that the attendants be informed of these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	If he grasps the vein too tightly, if the wound is too wide, for this reason it is necessary that the attendants be informed of these matters. And if he grasps it too tightly for the first time, that is good; but if this does not suffice, he must begin again, slightly loosening the grasp or the patient will faint.</start_of_turn>
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the limb is swollen, and the patient sighs, letting go for a moment or two, do not bind the limb:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	By chance there will come apostemes; do not enter or bathe, but begin again when the bleeding has stopped.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	And if he loses a little blood, or if he has a wound without a visible cause and you doubt that there is not as much blood as you see, even if you are sure of the loss itself with all the flames directly above;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if he loses a little blood, or if he has a wound without a visible cause and you doubt that there is not as much blood as you see, even if you are sure of the loss itself with all the flames directly above; so too does this often happen when the wound is small.</start_of_turn>
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the limb inflamed, if you do not renew the bleeding, put on a little oil of lavender, for it smoothens the pain of blood, and is mild in this limb the oil that is on it.</start_of_turn
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And thus apply the leech of oil to the wound that has bled, to staunch the course of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	And thus this same thing makes the wound tremble and swell up, when it is put on the limb; if it is too thick it will tear when it is too large.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there comes a large abscess, which has happened many times, even though it is not very deep,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	because if you open it too wide,
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	And you must know that you must do this after the evacuation of blood from the vein, and if it remains in place after a few days, neither black nor green mark will appear; if it does not harm me.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you see, do not put anything of aloes or myrrh moistened in juice of alum, mustard, or similar things.</start_of_turn>
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there is abscess and appearance to the blood of the basilisk: put your hand there, and if you find the limb soft under the compression of the hand, if that is the bad appearance.</start_of_turn
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Except that you do not put anything of what we have said, for by chance in court without an artery; but you must do indeed plaster dry to harden the limb, then treat it with another treatment, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to the quantity of its virtue and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if it is black, leave it be until it is red; and if you see it large, leave it until it is subtle; and if it is too thick, leave it cool down.</start_of_turn>
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is proper for the blunt and firm, and has the business of extracting blood, to make the wound larger and the flame greater.</start_of_turn
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for the weak one, make it the opposite, and make it healthier rather than worse, and you must make it healthier by cutting across, not by pricking.</start_of_turn
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this method of bleeding is useful for preventing the discharge of blood and for calming nerves, and is worth more than blood that remains long rather than wide.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for him for whom the flesh requires blood, it is to be given soft bread soaked in the juice of green apples; if he is faint, give him blood twice or thrice.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if he is of a cold complexion, let him beforehand eat soft bread soaked in honey or in aromatic honey with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and fragrant honey.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if he sweats after the discharge of blood, it is to be understood that he should drink broth of barley, and fragrant broth that smells like herbs,
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And use other things that we have said in the section or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he sees it is going to vomit again, and is well another time, if it is caused by great bleeding, he must rest and lie still, as much as he can
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who vomits after the first bleeding and has a strong pulse, if he rests for nine hours after the first bleeding or after the twelfth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who is well otherwise, if he must be well in two days or three
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the discharge of blood from a wound which has already been evacuated, and causes fever; if one can bear to remove a great quantity, and dilate the opening so that it bleeds profusely.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	having removed all the blood, and placing your hand over the wound while it is still bleeding, so that no more blood comes in its place.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this often happens when the patient is negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and you must not attempt to pull the limb out once it has been dislocated, but must press firmly on the wound to stop the bleeding again.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	If the limb is crooked, extend your arm strongly, for this would be bad.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but leave it as long as it remains whole the second time; or you point at the tip of the flame, until it has completely consumed the contents of the vein, which is enough to burst open.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put upon it some water and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has escaped, if you leave it and do not restrain it, until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessary, it is good to drain blood a second time, if the same is in the same limb, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The blood in the arm is pale in comparison to the vein of the shoulder because it is composed of it.</start_of_turn>
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the color of the blood is that of the patient's hand when it is in warm water, as long as the flesh is red.</start_of_turn>
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Then it should be bound firmly, if the vein opens well, and the same now through, not too wide or long;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	And let the wound be large, or be very close to the wrist joint; and if it cannot be closed, if you restore the hand to its natural position, let the blood flow freely until you have enough;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	And if it is thus, if you do not return the hand to its normal position in warm water, for more blood will flow into it than in this state.</start_of_turn>
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	The blood of this vein is more useful than all the others, for there is neither artery nor nerve.</start_of_turn>
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The saliva of the right hand is worth against all the diseases of the liver, and this is the method:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Strain the hand, and hold it in hot water, until the vein escapes if it is seen.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if the vein runs through, and you grasp it all the way round, if it does not bleed;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	do not go too deep, for the nerves are exposed without flesh,
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	then put the hand back in hot water, if it is not frozen in the wound, and do not move it.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the wound as well as you can, if you put oil on the vein or abscess and keep it warm, and do for every wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The blood in the left hand is worth the disease of mice, and do the same as I have said before concerning the right side.</start_of_turn>
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The blood of the armpit is worth for all the diseases that are upon the body.</start_of_turn
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	such as the disease of the marrow, retention of flowers, the disease of the rains, and of the veins, and of the old legs, and similar diseases.</start_of_turn>
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And if the patient has a wound that is somewhat filled with hot water, and wets on the wound until it blanches,
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	then he must keep the limb immersed in hot water until it turns white, and wipe it dry from the joint down to the ankle; and if it is at the elbow, from the elbow down to the hand there will be plenty of pus.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	the wound will be dry or even yield pus, or at the ankle, where the limb is bent, that there is a great flow of pus.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you wash the wound on the limb, if you take care of the nerves which are outside, and if you move the limb as if you were combing; and let the flame go out.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot be moved, if you reset the limb in the water, and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	If it must be forced, do it the first time; if you do it again, it will be in vain, for the limb is already salted.</start_of_turn>
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt, as we have said, and make the other limb equal.</start_of_turn>
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The limb of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of force, and its blood is worth the pain of the groin, when it is for blood that has clotted.</start_of_turn
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And if the patient is between or bathing, and strains below the ankle three times,
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	then the vein will not open; and if it does open, do so in all ways you can, and across.</start_of_turn>
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	it is better to leave it alone, for the liquid is thick, and it is easily returned by hand.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	and if you do not find it, if any rain of it escapes or remains stuck, and towards the little toe, and you are wary of the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And do as much correction of blood as you see, then loosen the connection, and put on a bandage and hold; it is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	It is now healed.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventouses are made of horn, or cobwebs, or glass; and are applied according to two methods: either by cutting and drawing out blood, or by cutting alone.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this method of applying the cautery if done according to two methods: either it is with great heat, or with less heat;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	And the wounds made by the cutting and extraction of blood, if they are made in twelve days, cause pain.
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	And the wounds made by the cutting and extraction of blood, if they are made in twelve days, cause pain, for in this case one is all at the head; and the other is in the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	And there are also three others in the twelve costae of the neck; and the wound causes swelling of the chin.
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	And the wound causes swelling of the armpits; and swelling on the shoulders;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	And the blisters cover half the arms; and the blisters cover half the legs.
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	And the blisters cover half the ankles; and the swelling does not affect blood, except for little veins that are scattered in the flesh,
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	Therefore it does not cause pain, as if we were bleeding from a vein;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	It is not painful, as if we were bleeding from a vein; and it is not to be administered with fire or any sensation of heat, in any disease caused by excess, until all the corrupted matter is evacuated.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if necessity demands it, or by custom, if the attendants bring a woman into the chamber during the course of a month, at the beginning or at the end, and every time she is there,
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	because there are some who, when they must speak, have a heavy head.
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are some who have swelling and redness in their face, and in their head, and at the throat, and their eyes are dull.
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and there are some who have a drop of blood in their mouth, and have lost their tongue, and spit blood.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if I have those who think, and see by no blood and no wound and blood and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and indeed when moisture is in the air, we command them to wait for two hours before they can go outside.</start_of_turn>
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The blood of the physician helps with the pain of the head … that comes from these ulcers, and we must only do this after the evacuation of all the flesh;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	The fire should not be more than 30 palms high, and never be bigger.
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	And it must not be done by anyone who is of a cold complexion or who has a hangover, for this causes great discomfort.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And for this reason it must not be done by anyone who is suffering from a cold temperament or who has a hangover.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And he who is sick in temperament, if he becomes unconscious, and for this reason it must be placed a little lower by the doubt of unconsciousness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The application of the ventouse below the chin is in place of the blood of the head and the marrow, and for this reason it is worth more than the greatest value,
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	And at a fissure of the windpipe towards the tonsils, and at a swelling, and at repletion.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And it is obvious that the swelling will burst, for if it remains too tightly, it will obstruct speech or eating or both.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The windsings cause pain in the chest as well as coughing and vomiting, and strangulation, and toothache.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	It is in lieu of the blood of the veins; and you must command the patient to express his hand to place it, that he does not pierce the artery, and does not bleed excessively.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The winds of the south blow low over the mouth, and at the corruption of the gums, and similar diseases which are in the mouth; and it is in the power of the healing of the twelve leaves.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The winds of the south blow low over the mouth, and at the corruption of the gums, and similar diseases which are in the mouth; and it is in the power of the healing of the twelve leaves.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The winds of the south blow low over the mouth, and at the corruption of the gums, and similar diseases which are in the mouth; and it is in the power of the healing of the twelve leaves
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The winds of the south blow low over the mouth, and at the corruption of the gums, and similar diseases which are in the mouth; and it is in the power of the healing of the twelve leaves
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	And instruct the patient not to fear too much pain, for the blood vessels are numerous, and he knows of bones and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The swelling that is on the buttocks is worth as many bruises at the foundation, and as diseases of bones, and it is known that the swelling should be great, and of a coarse texture, that it must be thoroughly treated; and by chance, if it should happen to be superficial, if it breaks, it will cause great wounds.</start_of_turn>
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The swellings of the legs swell widely open, because they draw blood from all parts of the body, and cause old wounds of the rains, and of the marrow, and of the bladder, and reduce the flowers; and are in place of the upper jowls, and of the calves, and all of them cause the body to swell afterwards along its length, and cause vomiting in various conditions.</start_of_turn
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	When the vacuum is placed first thing empty, and then with moderate warmth, put it on the patient immediately, and move it equally, and do not cease doing so until you see a little redness of the flesh and blood; then stop, and remove the vacuum, and take care of the body, for there are many who have suffered with this, and clear pores: if you do but wound once only, you will make large wounds and deep incisions; do it gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	If it is not too large, if you must wound it, do so but once: the first time to staunch the flow of blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	If it is very thick, if you must wound it, do so but three times; and when our wings draw blood from the wound, if we are only slightly wounded once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if our veins burst with blood, if we repeat this often; and if it is not expected, if we are in pain, we must finish if we suspect the cause is recognized.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And it is fitting for those who have thick skin and tough hair, and who have large pores, that you wipe away the pus of the oily aperitif and dissolving poultices:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is like this, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	or if it is ivy, with cumin oil, or heather, or chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	If excessive sweating is great and cold, take oil of marigold, or balsam, or oil of angelica, and the like.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	If the skin is pale and has large pores, do not put on oil,
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but must wash afterwards with rosewater, or cold water, or chamomile water, or cucumber water, or vinegar water, or some such thing.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And if anyone has a moist mouth, if he gets up easily, or from mistletoe, and sumac, and the like things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have superfluous swellings rise from wine strong, or from the water of sow, or from decoction of elderberry or chamomile, or from other such things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and do not remember to keep the patient still before or during the bath, but after the bath for an hour or so; and do not let them sleep after the ventosation.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and must be warned when they must be ventosated and when they are ventosated.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware those who are sickly are cold, and those who are too hot and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	If it is known that he has taken cold things, as apples, grapes, radishes and lettuce at ease, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and meat juice, mustard, broth of broth, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And whoever has a cold complexion, if he takes syrup of honey, and fragrant wine middle between vinegar and oil, and broth, and broth juice and small oils and herbs;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and when the wind is blowing, he must drink more than he eats.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	And you must give no more alms to anyone at any time frivolous or mischievous before or after, in order to comfort the principal limbs.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And be discreet about it, but do not let anyone know who is worthy of alms except those who truly deserve them.</start_of_turn>
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The wounds which are made for the application of the venouse are those which are made upon the liver, and upon the spleen, and under the tongue, and upon the belly and the buttock, and the armpit and the groin, for in these parts the limb does not suffer wounds upon the bones.</start_of_turn>
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and it is done only to draw blood from limb to limb,
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	If we put on the thumbs when they do not swell; to remove the viscosity that is in the limb, if we put on compresses on the belly and the buttocks to make the limb more flexible.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and loosen the pain, when there is a swelling or a stone, if you loosen by its natural attraction from an accident the swelling, or take out the stone from its place
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and make it limp when you put it on the liver and the heel when there is retained moisture.
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these compresses are administered empty so as to suck as little as possible; and never are administered together with fire, and never completely filled with water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	If there are diseases of the chest or in such a way that the wound is filled with hot water, or water, or where there are herbs covering that.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the wound administered with fire is thus:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	It has two inches of width and half an inch of depth, and has or comes out towards the middle like a pierced wound, just like a wound caused by a needle,
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	or be placed on the front if it does not bleed the patient when placed on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	And he has in the middle a stick of wire or iron, to put a bandage around.
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	And there are great and small ones according to the diseases and the severity of those who take them
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the wounds of the veins are different from those of the intestines, and the lean from the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And must one put this bandage upon the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	Take the candle or line and put it into the suction cup through the hole in the suction cup.
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	If it sticks at the bottom of the suction cup, it will not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it on the limb, and you must keep it either above or below the hole we mentioned above, so that when you see it, if there is vapor, withdraw the suction cup immediately.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and take hold of the candle or line as before, and do it often, if you must.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the case of a pleural effusion, which is administered for chest pain, there is no need for a vein or an incision, and it is only administered when it is in a state of acute inflammation, and is placed upon the limb as gently as possible.
et c’est li forme:	it is in this form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	They are only administered in members or where it is not possible to put on a ventouse because of their small size, such as livers and gums, and similar things.
