et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in the case of wounds without hair, such as boils or nails, and other similar things;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	And if you observe that the joints that are in soft and smooth movement do not make sense to you, take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	And put them into gentle water, until they are well-acquainted, and do not have anything in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	Then either keep the vein open with a ligature and a vacuum, and then rub the limb until it is red, and place the bandage on it;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	And when they are full and swell, and if it is possible to put on a vacuum, put it on, for this is worth doing afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, raise the limb easily, then with force, move it well, and then release it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the limb remains too long after the hair has been plucked, if moist, i.e. a bundle of linen in cold water, put on, until the hair is stretched out;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the hair is multiplied, put on broken glass, or nails, and similar things, until it is stretched out.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you put out half of the beans peeled, and let them burn on the limb, if you stop it now.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if you have more pain, take other unguents.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the unguents do not suffice, rub the limb with fresh blood, or insert a needle into it until the pain ceases.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	Then apply them once more, and as soon as they feel relief from the pain, if they bleed;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see that they bleed, sprinkle some powder of aloes and saffron over them, or charcoal, if they will now stop bleeding.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Ci comence li livre des brisures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is the restoration of fracture and displacement.</start_of_turn>
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Listen well, dear son, for this chapter teaches you something that none of the old books have ever mentioned, no letter has ever written.</start_of_turn
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	Therefore, in our land, this science is strange, for I have never found anything like it before.</start_of_turn
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	And I know of nothing else, save by the science of ancient books, or because I have studied so much that I have treated this science, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	I have described in this chapter what is contained in this book, and I have abbreviated it at the end, and I have made it clear the forms of the instruments which are mentioned, as I have done in the preceding chapters
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore it is necessary that we say or write in the prologue of this book the sum of the word and the chapters or the sayings which put understanding into it, and remain on the truth, so that those who are proven to be learned may learn this noble art and learn it from others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twist or sprain occurs to anyone, if you must hasten the patient to a physician from one side to the other, if nothing else hinders you, if from weakness of body, infancy, or old age;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if he is too weak, or too cold; and eat only cold broth, that is to say cold broth, broth of herbs and vinegar, and drink no wine, eat no fatty foods, and do not fill the stomach too much with meat, until you are certain that the patient will not suffer from excessive bleeding, or swelling of the limb; if he recovers, let him rest first for a moment before continuing treatment.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the fractured bone begins to heal, if you must order the patient to eat meat which causes great swelling, or if it has viscosity, as with wheat flour in water, and rye, and testicles, and spleen, and pancreas, and fish, and large wine, and similar things.</start_of_turn>
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For in part of nourishment, muscle and bone grow more brittle.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	Therefore, bones broken from marrow and decrepit ones do not mend well because of the drying out of the limbs, just as bones that are too brittle;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but it is healed by large tensions which hold the limb together, as much as they are strong; and it does not cause any damage, so it is recommended to feed on strong foods, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And it is observed that fractures are of various kinds in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot, or of the arm, and I shall tell you in this chapter all the ways of fracture.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go to the marrow, and others by bending, as with the size of a nail to write with.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with a small tear.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And concerning the bruise of the breast has its means, and its own instrument in restoring, according to what he remembers comes to his mind;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And it is known that a fracture of the bone is caused by that which twists the limb, and it opens well by pushing, and sometimes by the pressure of the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when there is no swelling or touch, and the patient does not feel much pain, there is no fracture;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can well have swelling, or fissure, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you do not know how to move the limb, but put on medicines that will come later, and then strain it gently now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And the threads that break that go into the marrow, and are the third parts of the joints, it is now necessary to put them in order equally, even as after incisions remain.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if incisions remain, if you leave them without care, as long as the incisions are still inflamed;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then put them in order with the muscles that you must gently and prudently stretch, and the threads that restore them are lighter than those of other parts; then restrain, as it is necessary afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if there are broken pieces in the bone, if they are two parts, if they are hands or feet, or at your hand if it is a small limb, or at two strings, or at a string and at your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	And set the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the limb break, remain by all means the adjuncts of its flesh to the muscle as you wish, and keep that by your work there comes no lesion or pain to the patient.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And adjust well the joints of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel well with the hand if you think that it is not well: if the wound is healing well, and it is not strained too much, do not press as those who do who make it come by their work to swelling and contraction in the limb, as we have often seen
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is at a point, if the patient is truly sick and does not move it, neither awake nor asleep, neither turning nor in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and take great care that the limb is firmly secured so that it feels no pain at all.</start_of_turn>
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it feels no pain, if it is not at a point, and you must put it in a position where it feels no pain.</start_of_turn>
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and keep it straight, so that there is no twisting when you restore it.</start_of_turn>
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	And as for the quality of a broken limb, that is as I have said.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The quality of a broken limb is diverse in small and large pieces and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small limbs, such as bones and thumbs and the like: if you cover them with linen cloth and silk;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those which are large, such as thighs and legs and arms: if you cover the limb with coarse linen cloth and silk;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then lie down and stretch your limbs lightly, two or three according to the limb, and strain your hand one palm to the other, then go up to the break and strain less, than the break then dislocate one palm from the break.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the limb one palm and the other, as much as you grasp a great part of the limb, then take hold of another limb, and turn the shoulder back in place over the limb that is broken
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then raise to the lower part of the break, and strain moderately, neither too strong nor too weak, as we said earlier;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then put between the layers of staples, linen or cloths, as many as are even; and bind them together with bands, and then put your pins well made above, if there is no incision or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or incision, if you put above soothing things that calm the incision, and which hold the swelling, and leave them in place for some days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then strain above your pins, and let them be half the width of a broad thumb ring, or of a clove of fennel, or of barleycorns, and let them be in this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But it is necessary that the staple which is put on the fracture be larger and broader than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	And be of equal length as it is necessary for the limb in its entirety or in its breadth
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	Then is strained upon the staples as you did at the first hour, and then bind under a thread that will remain firm, as in the first hour on the fracture;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	more is tight, the less; and it is necessary that the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, and be of linen wool.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For if the threads are thick, as I have seen fools do who bind their wounds with linen cord, it is a great mistake, for the cord will not be even if it is too fine, and it will not hold securely unless there is some space between the stitches.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is bruised by the blows of the stones after the stretching of their bones, if you put sponges of linen or coarse cloth on them, they will not swell up.</start_of_turn>
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the fracture, and the bone is broken, I shall speak of the cure for that later.</start_of_turn>
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And the threads that he cannot bear to hold are those which break first of all.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limb is large, he cannot bear to put these [stitches] except after five or seven days, or more according to your suspicion of the wound coming out;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And when the old plaster must restore a fracture, dislocation, and torsion: take a little flour that is held as by the walls of a mill, and mix it with much egg, and make this confection, not too thick not too thin, and use it; for this is the common method of plastering which restores the fracture in many positions, and even among women and small children, for it is neither too harsh nor too rough.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plastering that restores the fracture and dislocation and torsion: take three barley grains and linseed, mugwort, asafoetida, gum arabic, and mastic, in all; myrrh and aloes, in two; aloe vera, in seven; and grind them together, and mix them with egg white; for if the patient's complexion is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition and restores the broken bones very quickly, and is worth more than many homes.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Other method of displacement worth torsion: take mugwort and vismut, 3 each; mix with mire and aloes, 8 each; acacia, 5 each; arnica, 10 each, and grind well, and confit with water or abundant oil, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Other method of displacement worth torsion: take mugwort and vismut, 3 each; mix with mire and aloes, 8 each; acacia, 5 each; arnica, 10 each, and grind well, and confit with water or abundant oil, and administer. The plaster does not restore immediately, but it is good for soothing post-cautery pain, and the bones properly the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Other method of displacement that restores fractured bones: take dried fig tree leaves and terrestrial pellwort leaves, and grind together, and make plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Other methods of restoring the fracture of the bone and removing the remaining abscess. Take root of vismalve, chamomile, violets flowers, wheat flour, and nutmeg one part; and grind, and mix with wine, and if the limb is swollen, mix with vinegar of coriander moist, or vinegar alone, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Other methods of support are more forceful than the first, when a hard abscess comes with the restoration of the limb. Take root of vismalve, flaxseed, barley, melilot, violets and chamomile flowers, all of one part; and grind, and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates in his book does not put anything on the broken limb to restore it except for some fat and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be between two and not too soft or too hard
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen recommends putting something dry and warm on the broken limb, such as myrrh, aloes, incense and the like, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way of dressing that is worth for pain and swelling: take mugwort and chopped onions, or poppy seeds, and mustard, and mix them evenly, and grind them, and make a dressing of it and bind it.</start_of_turn>
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	Then loosen a little afterwards, and take care that the patient feels no pain, that the bone is not displaced; if you do not loosen by hand for a while.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain comes to the limb, or swelling or itching, if you hasten, and loosen it, and support the limb in place; and take a light bandage, and a sponge of salt and moisture, and immerse in water, and elevate the limb, until the itching ceases, and the pain is calmed.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then leave the limb rest for an hour, and put on dry linen, soaked in water or rose oil, and bind up with a knot, until you are certain of the healing of the wound
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And rest the inflamed limb, and relieve the pain, then bind up again with a soft bandage, and a little more of support, and do not bind too tightly; and be discreet until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see swelling, redness, pain and swelling around a bone, and if there is a recurrence, you must repeat the procedure as you did the first time.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	If there is no improvement in the limb after the things we have mentioned, if it does not straighten out after two or three or five or seven days, do not leave it for twenty days, as we have seen; until the fracture has healed, and the limb is brought back into its natural position.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Therefore you must support it more strongly than before, and nourish the limb as I mentioned earlier; and if you see that the limb is drying out more than usual, do not attempt to force moisture into it, for it will not help.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	The fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	When the fire cautery is used, do not remove the dressing from the limb too quickly; and do not be hasty in handling the matter, for if you do, you will make the matter worse, and if you are uncertain, I do not see anything better than to leave it alone and treat it directly.</start_of_turn>
des diverses manieres de brisure	various methods of fracture.</start_of_turn
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many methods of fracture, and various figures, and the causes are diverse.</start_of_turn
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For there are fractures that are made by the percussion of a spear, and the collar of bone is fractured throughout to the syfac which is the socket of the bone, as is done by a saw or an axe; and for this reason this kind of fracture is called a fracture of the bone.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or if the spear pierces the bone in a reverse direction, it is called this kind of fracture 'absolute'; and there are wounds of these two kinds, great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded percussion, or fracture or collar of bone, or fracture of bone on bone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture that approaches the socket which is below the bone, or it is above the bone, and is this wound, or large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound is filled with bone as densely as a braid, and the fracture is small, it is called a "capillary" fracture.
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is made by a pierce, or by cutting, or by a similar thing, and if it makes the bone marrow enter, and if the limb is as limp as when broth is boiled on pots; if the marrow comes between the bones.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this has more under it that those who have drunk too much wine; like children who have drunk too much.
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And thus in all these ways of fracture, small pieces are detached from them as with stars; and I will speak of it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And thus in all these ways of fracture, small pieces are detached from them as with stars, and the tension on the tense parts, and the corrupt matter that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The blood vessel is known by this that when we have discovered the bone, and we wipe grease over it, if the black fracture is opened
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, take care of the patient’s ailments, and if you see no other mishap, as vomiting of bile, emission of urine, extension, and swelling, and fever, and the eyes turning yellow and red, and other similar things in various situations, if you cannot otherwise make sense of it.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	If you do not see an imminent accident, and you hope for health, if so, begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	When the limb comes first to you, and that is in the armpit, if so, it is best to remove the bone from the fourth space above the muscle as you do.</start_of_turn>
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in this state, if you hurry to remove the bone from the seventh space above the bone, so that the marrow of the bone is corrupted, comes the accident that we have mentioned.</start_of_turn>
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the breaking of the bone comes up to the marrow that covers the brain, if so, you must make an opening in the part that is broken: and that is that you take hold of the head of the patient and uncover the bone in all the ways that you can, and on the figure of the wound more severe than you can.</start_of_turn
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And if blood comes out when uncovering the bone, or incisions are made, let him hold what he can to his aid; and fill the wound with cloths soaked in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And rest the wound until the incisions are healed; then when the bleeding has stopped, begin to bind up the bone steadily. This is done in three ways: the first way is if the tail of the incision is narrow in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then there is another incision which is greater than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And thus if you have many different sizes of boils, some are soft and some are hard, and are pointed, and of iron inde; and in a slight wound, do not lance the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is firm and hard, if you must pierce through, do not make holes except where the bone actually breaks through; and must have above the point a margin or circle, which does not leave the point pass beyond the bone; and you must have several of these, so that the flesh comes out in place of the thickness of the bone, if you have holes throughout the test; and this is the form of the two methods of holes.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing through the bone is that you put in a tarer on the bone, and twist your two hands until you feel that the bone is pierced; then put the tarer back in another place a little later, and do everything around, and close the incisions of the space between the holes, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you have moved the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have like pins or tweezers; and keep your hand away from the brain and the jaw.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced the bone, and treated, if it is possible, reset the fragment which has broken away from the bone to all other instruments which are like an incisor, but it must be firmer and more flexible than the others.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And if it has not fractured any of the small bones, no teeth, if the bone is slightly fractured with some instruments; then cure the wound with sutures and bandages as we have mentioned.</start_of_turn>
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of treatment is like that of the Galenicians, which is more reliable; and the lord is very strong, and that is his word.</start_of_turn
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is proper first that you uncover a portion of the bone, either the fracture or break open muscle, so that when you have uncovered that portion, you must place the index finger of your left hand over the pointed end of this incisor lens, as follows:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	Do not pierce from one side only, but rather from the edge of the joint, so that if you pierce through the bone; then take hold of a little mallet above, so that you gently press the bone around, and take care of the surrounding tissue that is below.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is tough against the bone, if the bone is slightly bent, because one must well feel it when it is badly injured, and feel no pain.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	If the bone breaks without piercing the skin, cut the bone as little as possible; there are small pieces remaining. If it is possible to rejoin them, do so with the blunt end of a scraper, using various quantities as needed, to fill each cavity adequately according to the work and the nature of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If there is abundant scraping beforehand, and afterwards more subtly, and it does not cease to do so until it is well done
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In small cuts of other sizes and breaks that are subtle, it is prudent to provide the cause according to its location; and this is something that is not mentioned in this art by anyone who has put their study into this area.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is discovered, you must take one drape of linen, according to the extent of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and place it upon the wound.
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then take another drape of linen doubled in half or in quarters, soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it upon the first drape; and make it more gentle than you would, that you do not damage the wound further. Then administer from above another piece of linen, and do not tighten it more than is necessary to hold the wound in place only.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and leave it thus for one or two days until the swelling subsides, then remove it, and administer medications such as roots of ivy, alum, and incense, and arnica, and similar things; from these things make powder, and put it upon the wound, and administer appropriate medications as before.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And beware that the wound be perfectly closed, that you do not leave it open, neither do you leave it gather bones together, for when bones gather together on the soft brain, if they bind and swell, it brings great harm to the patient; for when one puts upon the surface of the wound something biting, if it does not desist from below.

Then come the treatments in various ways that are appropriate, as long as it is healthy. The veins that are never broken in two parts do not bleed, or bleed only slightly; for these are bones; and when cartilage is involved, it does not break unless something forces it to bulge or twist, and then it is well healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the parts is broken, if you should swallow your little finger or the hole of your thumb, and put the break back into your index finger and the wrist in turn, until it returns to its natural shape.

de la routure de la mandibule	De la routure de la mandibule.
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement. If movement of the jaw comes loose, or is dislocated, if it is strained by a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put upon the broken jaw a cerote, and put upon it a double drape; and upon the drape a great staple well made, or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the jaw, and bind it upon the muscle as you please, and command the patient to rest, and feed him soft food.

Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if the abscess comes out, if it is as we have said many times before.

de la forcele	forcefully
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceful fracture occurs many times before, behind the shoulder, and the fracture is according to two methods: when it is broken and desevree in three parts, and there are pieces, and it is the lightest to restore; or if there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And when the fracture is towards the wound, you must have two assistants, one of whom will hold the limb that feels the forceful fracture; and the other will extend the collar towards the part; then put the fracture back in place, so that it forms as it should, and there is no sign or swelling.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you have to extend further, put under the patient’s shoulder a round ball of lead, or cloth, as thick as you need; and hold and keep the forceful fracture steady, and strain the ball with your hand, so that you can put the fracture back in place as it should.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez. et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and seems like a scoop, and is neither thick nor thin, and be as wide as it should be, according to the size of the bone and the ability of the work; and has two holes, as you see, and one is large, and the other is small, as is the course of the wound that you made when you treated the bones;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are assured of the depth of the wound, if the wound is small, or if you doubt the depth, if you employ a dressing and a bandage, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	If the wound has bled, if it is small, take oil of roses, assails, and wine, and put on top.</start_of_turn>
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The hardening of the bone, when it has wounds and senses of the tailor, is that you put on the bone the plaster of the powder of the mill and the yolk of an egg, and put on a bandage, and put a sponge under the armpit if necessary.</start_of_turn>
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very great bandage of a broad palm, then put on a double drape over the wound, and support it; then take a slender needle of two palms wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage, so that the head of the bandage remains in place.

de la brisure de l’espaule	Then resume the displacement, if you see that it is necessary, and hold and leave it in place until it is restored; and it is usually restored within .xxviij. days, and in fewer than most homes.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, or if the limb is too large to fit through, do not force it out; if the limb appears according to the shape of the dislocation, reduce it according to its natural form in every way that you can; then put on the limb powder with plenty of eggshell, and bandage firmly, and put on a wide and soft cushion, a little wider than the shoulder, and if the cushion slips from the shoulder, use a bandage of flaxseed, so that the cushion rests evenly; and then hold firmly at a great bend, so that the cushion does not move from its place, and watch the limb carefully; and every time it relaxes, if you hold it, and put it back in place if it has moved from its place, and keep the patient lying down; and the shoulder is restored in .xx. days or less.  And when this number is completed, if the limb is flexible, and so be sure, for it is not the bone that easily recovers.

de la brisure dou pis	And if a piece of the bone sticks out beforehand, and does not yield like before, if it persists, hold the bone steady and do what we said in the breaking of the forceps to soothe the abscess.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. The limb is never broken in the middle, but this happens often; but it often breaks on exertion. Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez. Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois. de la brisure de l’ajutoire	De la brisure de l’ajutoire.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is the one between the shoulder blade and the ball of the shoulder, and if it is dislocated, it must be restored in one of two ways: which is to take a fistful of myrrh, as follows:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And as two fingers are bent, two thumbs are bent, and hold the patient above a seat; then grasp the limb with the fist, until it reaches the armpit, and put in the middle of the fist a corb of the fist, then put on no weight or the attendants extend downwards; then put the joint back in its place, as it should be.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that you support the patient on his shoulder, and you bind the arm to his collar, and order the attendants that one of them holds what is on the joint at his hands, and the other holds downwards at all the bones, and stretch the scapulae outwards.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. If the extraction is too violent, if it strains, that is, if it tears the flesh, on the base and on the top, extend thumbs of the assistants to their side. And if the fracture is close to the shoulder-blade, it is necessary to insert, that is, to place, the middle finger between the scapula and the bone; and in the same way if the fracture is towards the elbow, it is necessary to insert, that is, to place, the little finger between the scapula and the bone; and just as if the fracture is between the elbow and the shoulder-blade, if it is possible, place the little finger lightly, with effort, until the fracture is even on both sides of the bone and the shoulder-blade; then place the fracture evenly, if possible, and strain, if necessary, because the after-effects will not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez. If you doubt that the bone is not moving, use splints, and on the fracture put on a splint that is wider and stronger than the others, and have between the splints a space of about two finger-widths; and let one splint be as large as to pass over the fracture two finger-widths; then strain on the splints, as I have said above concerning the chapter on the fracture, stronger and less flexible.

de la brisure du bras	In the event that the shoulder joint has been dislocated due to moisture, and has been reset but remains unstable, resulting in recurrent dislocations with even slight movement, as we have observed, you must first stabilize the dislocation.
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm consists of twelve bones, which are called the "femurs," of which one is small and is the one that supports the pouch; and the other is large, and is the one that is hollow, towards the little toe; by chance the large femur only breaks, or the small, and by chance they break together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small femur is fractured, the restoration is easy, and the healing; but when the large is fractured, if the healing is bad, it is more painful than when they are fractured together. If only the small femur is fractured, if the limb is slightly extended, and made even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it is the large femur that is fractured, if the limb is strongly extended; and it is supported on one cushion, and the pouch of the hand is held higher than the other, and the small is lower than the others, and the patient's hand is crossed over itself, and the cushion is placed in front of it higher than the patient's hand; then the patient does not suffer any pain. Then extend the limb at the shoulder to the part below the hand, or to the elbow, and one other hand at the other side above. And then put the limb in its normal position, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	If it breaks into pieces, if you put some together in its place, and if there is no displacement that has pierced or torn it, you shall not be able to restore it to its place, for it will remain fractured as before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	If with the fracture there is a wound, as I have already mentioned in this chapter; take the cure.</start_of_turn>

And let the bandages over the fracture be soft and moist, neither too hard nor too rough; and let the thread used for the pins be neither too thick nor too thin. de la brisure de la main	Of the fracture of the hand

de la cuixe brisie	of the broken limb
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.
