Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	The patient lies on his face, then extends his limbs symmetrically; and it is when the fracture is fixed to the bone
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the fracture is close to the thigh bone, if either of the limbs above the knee or the other limb below the fracture is fractured; and in the same way if it is close to the knee, and then either the limb above the knee or the lower limb; then put the thumbs of both hands at the same level as the limb, until it is according to its natural figure, and then put on the dressing and bind it, without causing any further damage.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	If there is swelling above the wound, if you leave it quiet and return to your work and your cure, the ligation is made hastily.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	If there is swelling above the wound, if you leave it quiet and return to your work and your cure, the ligation is made hastily. It is necessary to wrap around the limb with a strong bandage, doubled in two or three places, and to keep the excess taut, then to draw up the limb until the nails reach the root of the nail, and to pass through between the heel and the limb, above the kneecap, and under the heel bone, and to draw up the limb and the bandage on the heel, then to put on the outer bandage and an external splint, and to place a splint on the bone of the limb; and to employ between the limb and the bandage several layers of soft cloth to make equal the tension, and to begin to tie in two or three places on the bandage; and as you go on adding more to the bandage, reduce the tension; then take out two or three stitches that you passed between the limb and the bandage, and tie two external stitches that are below, and replace at the top with the needle, until you see that the swelling has gone down; and the tension, if it does not move from its place, then leave it alone, and do not cause any other swelling or wound.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If there is swelling above the wound, if it comes loose, and you address what has come, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that prick, it is necessary to remove them, if possible; and if that is not possible, it is necessary to cut the limb open, and drain the pus. Treat the wound as we have said, as long as it is healthy.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is the bone broken in this case where it is set with pins, as in the arm or leg; nevertheless, in the restoration done in this way, I do not feel any pain in the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And the swelling that remains in the bone after it has been restored, lasts for one or two days, or less or more, according to the variations of complexion.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groin region.
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	The swelling in the groin region often breaks, but it often happens again. And if it breaks, it is no longer just a tear, or a perforation, but there is bleeding, pain, and this is well understood.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if restoration is to be made, set the round things that are round back to their place until they are properly assembled; then put on the dressing and put on a round splint, if you have need of it, and strain it as it should be strained; then reward all the arrangements that we have said above in other cases, as in the case of an abscess or other similar things; and if you put in each mishap what it should have, as long as it is sane.
de la brisure de la jambe	And if restoration is to be made, set the round things that are round back to their place until they are properly assembled; then put on the dressing and put on a round splint, if you have need of it, and strain it as it should be strained; then reward all the arrangements that we have said above in other cases, as in the case of an abscess or other similar things; and if you put in each mishap what it should have, as long as it is sane.
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	And if restoration is to be made, set the round things that are round back to their place until they are properly assembled; then put on the dressing and put on a round splint, if you have need of it, and strain it as it should be strained; then reward all the arrangements that we have said above in other cases, as in the case of an abscess or other similar things; and if you put in each mishap what it should have, as long as it is sane. Saiches that there are in the limb have two bones; one is called the "mustel" and the other is called the "foscile"; and there is every break as it comes to the arm, and because of this the restoration is just like that of the arm, and the work is all the same.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if two bones are fractured together, the limb is twisted from every part.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if a bone is fractured at its root, the limb is twisted forward
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if a large bone is fractured, if one feels great pain and sees it well fractured; then one must extend it, and set it even, and bind the fragments evenly; however, if the fracture is serious, and there are multiple pieces, it is better to extend slightly and more gently; and to adjust as you are able
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, if you take four strips of cloth that cover the limb from one side to the other, and be as long as the limb from the hip to the foot; then wrap around with four layers of lint around and below, and bind firmly in the middle, and to this bandage will not allow the limb to bend to the right or to the left, and that is good; and no one will administer anything more long than the limb, and if there is swelling, and it has several pieces, it is better to extend slightly and more gently; and to adjust as you are able.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the fracture of bones in general.
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture; but in bones of marrow there is never a fracture, and two must suffice, and there is no other treatment except for numerous positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture in bones of marrow, and you see these bones crushing one another, if you place the limb so that it would appear to be flying away, then put the limb on the ground, just as if it were falling, and then put the limb back in its place; then press until it returns to its original position; then put on the dressing and bandage, and put on a little stool under the belly of the limb, about an inch high, and strain the limb gradually, and when it has recovered, wrap it in bandages, and other things as you deem necessary
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when two or three days have passed, if the limb is still loose, because you will find the bones either broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	If there be any two breaks, if you restore them as we have said must be two-handed; then put at the break a splint according to the length of the break, and make it somewhat wider; then put on the thumb that I have mentioned, and strain immediately; and if there are three or more breaks, break them, and put on over each break a splint as per their quantity, wrapped in one layer of linen, and strain the thumb from the bone.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	Remember also the other things that I have said about other breaks; and secure each accident as it should be secured.</start_of_turn>
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the humerus bone.</start_of_turn>
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bones of the nature of a woman are broken, if she sits enlarged, then lean her towards the back; and hold her there by behind. Then fill the belly of the nature with cotton, and put as much as a sto on it. Then pull out the woman, and keep her back and front; and immediately jump the cotton out, until it comes to the entrance of the nature, and bring back the bone with the sto; and when she sees her piss, if she has pulled out the cotton, and when she has pissed, she will recover, and make face for seven days or more: if the fracture is restored, and if you see her, take a bladder of berbis, and tie a string around her belly, and empty the bladder into the nature; then blow through the string until the bladder is emptied: the nature will return the fracture; then fill it with cotton, and leave it alone for a few days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the bone of the arm of a man is broken, or of a woman, if you restore it as we have said concerning the thigh bone; and these fractures are not seen except by the one who puts his study and his work into it, and reads my book. For the fracture signifies in more ways the right way of restoration: then do so.</start_of_turn>
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the groin, when it is broken, take a goose beak and put it in the groin; then wrap it round with cloths, and leave it for two days or until it is healed.
de brisure avec plaie	Of sudden with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	In case of sudden fracture with wound, even if it is great, as with the bones of the thigh or shoulder or similar, that it be immediately set in order, if what we have said is true concerning these symptoms.</start_of_turn>
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is clean, if the vitriol has been delayed, if you have nothing else, then resume the reduction in this way at the same hour, or at the least as soon as possible, for if it is delayed, it will not be cured.</start_of_turn
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if there is swelling of the wound, if the fracture is not reduced until the swelling has gone down, do not touch either the third or the fourth part, for you will cause further harm.</start_of_turn
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	If the bone breaks suddenly, it is found outside the socket as if it had been discovered, then you must hold your hands lightly at the point of the break.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	If the limb extension does not appear to you in order to make them equal at your hands, if you have this instrument of iron which is about twelve or thirteen inches long, and the size is according to the quantity of the wound; and for this reason it is necessary at the mire that it grasps three or four inches, according to what is necessary in the wound of the fracture; and whether round or square, that it does not press too much on the limb at your work, and whether it is before or behind, and large in front, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	It is called "palainche" because it is necessary to place the curved limb over the apparent head of the bone; and once it is in place, it should be equal on both sides so that one meets the other. And if the fracture is slight and the instrument does not hold the bone well, if you press on the head of the bone, as long as the instrument has possession of it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot restore the bone, as we have said, if you are forced to apply an instrument that can cover this, such as a hook or saw, to your need; then remove that which remains embedded in the bone by scraping and removing the surrounding marrow.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	When the bone is restored, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, the swelling that has occurred will not be in its natural position. If you do nothing, it will swell further; then moisten it with black vinegar and keep it covered; do not put any cerote or other dressing on the wound, as this will cause putrefaction and corruption; then administer stars [medicinal herbs] when the bone has been restored, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover the dressing thoroughly, according to the size of the wound, and take care that the wound is not strained with the fracture; for many times this has been done foolishly, and has caused death or damage on many occasions; or at least it has rendered the fracture more painful and prolonged than others.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	If the wound is small or large, and you doubt that anything serious is wrong, as we have said, and you find pain in the limb; if you do not wish to put on stars [medicinal herbs], cover it thoroughly; but instead of stars, use firm bandages and tie them securely. And when you see afterwards that the swelling is diminishing, although there is still some pain, if you put on more stars than before, and if there is any ointment for wounds, such as ointment of tetrapharmacon and the like.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it must be that you bind the limb three times a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it must be that the limb is kept in its place as much as possible, so that it can heal easily
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	If it is displaced again, and cannot be rejoined in its place, with slight fractures that there are small pieces of bone, because it must be thought that you wish to close the wound, and reunite all these fragments of bone that cause this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	If an abscess comes to the bone, or another way of corruption, if you must cure it, as it is said in this chapter above. And when the bone is broken, and is open on the limb, as the bone of the thigh or the shoulder, and other great bones, if you do not treat it, for many times it will come to death, but leave it until it has healed; for it will surely disappear by itself after twenty or thirty days, and then cure the wound if you wish; or leave it alone.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	From the beard that comes out of the beard hair.
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	From the beard that comes out of the beard hair, we often see after the swelling of the wound, especially when it is near the joint, and it is helpful to see the figure of the limb; and by chance it cannot do its natural work
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore take care that you are aware: if you administer astringent medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocoll, acacia, and similar others, that you take none of these things, or all together, and mix them with a stifling wine or with plenty of egg or with buttermilk; and put them on the wound, and strain it well, and do not remove it from the hand for days; and then dislocate it, and repeat this until the nodes are bony; or you strain on a well-made piece of sponge; for the property of sponge is that it will harden all the swellings under the limb; and if the node has already hardened as much as a stone, and it is necessary to break it, if the swelling above is great, and to make the apparent superfluity disappear; or do not remove it from any wound, as long as it is bony, and cure it when it is healed
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	Weak limb after the bandage.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone is restored and the limb is weakened and limp, if there is any discomfort: sometimes this is because it was too tightly bound and was not properly loosed; or because there are too many bands, and it cannot regain its natural position; or because of many wounds; or because of too great a movement, not even in its hour; or because there is much blood in the body, if it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is to make the patient relax, and to make the limb firm, until the swelling is multiplied in him; and give him baths, and make him cheerful and comfortable; then put a poultice on the limb, so that the poultice attracts the great nourishment, and the wound often bleeds profusely, until the nourishment returns to the limb; and restore it to its natural position.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The limb is twisted after the blessing.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the bone is broken open, and the limb is deformed, although it does not lose its natural work: if one does not believe the fools who say that the limb must be broken anew, and many have done this in our land; this work is blamed, and great evils result, and by chance the patient; although if the nodulations and the torture are fresh, if you command that they be washed away with warm water, or with soft herbs be cooked, like leaves of chamomile, and roots, and meadowsweet, and similar things; and you make an application of a softening plaster, like good beeswax done, and you take the nourishment of chamomile, and confit with fat of gelly or oil of poppy seed, and apply the plaster again; or you take greasy figs, and grind them with dung of the colon, and similar medicines that appease the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And never is the bone loosened by continuous rubbing with wet hands. And either bring movement to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	If the dislocation is swollen and hardened, like a stone, and needs to be held by iron, if it is covered up to the bone, make an incision slightly deeper; and put padding and a bandage on the wound.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	If the dislocation is swollen and hardened, like a stone, and needs to be held by iron, if it is covered up to the bone, make an incision slightly deeper; and put padding and a bandage on the wound.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs without any apparent cause, if it is now necessary to restore its proper position.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	When it is delayed, if the limb is swollen, and by chance it is reset, there are often points on the limb; for this reason one must not move it while it is swollen: many times this causes spasms and other pains.</start_of_turn>
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	However, when this has happened, if you make the patient comfortable, then leave him, until the swelling has subsided; then raise the limb high and with oil, and then gently restore it, and cure each limb as it comes into its place.</start_of_turn
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations from the shoulder to the foot.</start_of_turn>
des mandibules	Des mandibules.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	The jaws. For the jaws are loosened and the dislocation of both is frequent: either because they are fixed to the bone of their roots, and softened a little; or because they are loosened entirely, and hang towards the chin, and tear the saliva from the mouth that it cannot hold it, cannot close its mouth, and engulfs its tongue with the word.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, if it returns by itself several times.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and accompanied, if you must, restrain it immediately, and do not delay;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And in such manner that the minister grasps the head of the sufferer, and holds the gaze fixed downwards from one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the mandible within the mouth, if the dislocation is three-quarters complete; and the other hand must be thrust out, to make them even; and command the patient to soften his mandibles and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the eye must be kept level, until it returns to its place.</start_of_turn>
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it returns grasped, even if both mandibles are together, if they are swollen with hot water and oil, so that they are kept lightly; do not attempt to force it back, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are returned even, and the patient’s mouth is closed with a gentle touch, if you put on moist cloths in cerote made of rose oil and wax, then bind them lightly with thread.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	And let the patient rest on their back, with their arms resting between two cushions, so that they do not move forward or backward, or to the side, without making an effort to move, but take hold of the meat firmly, until the pain is gone, and bind the jaw bones securely.</start_of_turn>
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And then let them gently chew what they see lightly, and do not work too hard to open their mouth to eat or drink, until the jawbone is well bound and healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	If the two jaw bones do not manage to return to their place at once, and are not firmly secured at their roots, if in comes fever and customary sickness, and by chance vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	When you see this, know that it is a loss; and many times death follows in eight days.</start_of_turn>
de la forcelle	of the forceps.</start_of_turn>
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot remove pain from the root of the tooth, and is valueless whenever it is applied with force, and it is well known.</start_of_turn
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And if the patient lies recumbent with his back on the ground, extend his arms; then press gently at the shoulder joint, and it will return; then place the bandage and dressing on the shoulder, and hold it in place.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	And the head of the shoulder, which is towards the chest, cannot be dislocated; if it does dislocate once, if he lets it go again, if he rests his arm, as we have said; then place the bandage and dressing on the shoulder, and hold it in place, and command the patient to rest until he is healed.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And in the same way, the dislocation of the shoulder is brought back to its place when the limb is freed from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	From the dislocation of the shoulder.
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	The shoulder is dislocated only by two means: firstly, that it comes out at the glenoid part; and secondly, at the head of the humerus; and sometimes at the root, and this is harmful.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Neither the back nor the front of the shoulder dislocates easily; and more often it comes out from below towards the glenoid part, even among those who have a lot of flesh; for among those who have little flesh, the dislocation comes out with force, and returns with force.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes there happen to be blows or fractures, and it swells the shoulder with a hot abscess, and one must take care that it is not dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is necessary indeed. As long as you are sure; then commence the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known that a dislocation is when it is tilted towards the shoulder blade, and it distinguishes between the diseased and healthy shoulder, and you will find between their difference the manifestation;
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and at the head of the shoulder there is a groove, and the shoulder blade touches the head of the shoulder, just as if it were a nail; and the patient cannot raise their arm to their side, or move in any way
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and also, if it is displaced upwards, if it is not hidden inside, because you find it clearly on touching;
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And this manner of dislocation is not useless to restore, when it is new, or when the limb is painful.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the physician grasps the painful limb high up, then places the thumbs below the armpit, and grasps the joint forcefully high up; and the physician grasps the limb and stretches it high up, because it places it below; if it comes immediately.</start_of_turn>
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it does not come as we have said above, if it is to be believed that the patient is to be bathed in warm water; and to administer soothing and softening medication, such as decoction of artemisia and fennel and honey in water, and to administer; </start_of_turn
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then either support the patient on his back, and put under the armpit a cushion of linen equal in size, not too soft nor too hard, and put the hand of the patient on the cushion, and keep the shoulder joint firmly, and treat the painful limb;
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	And another minister holds the patient’s head firmly in place, so that it does not move downwards; that space returns immediately, and if you see that it remains fixed in this way:
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and that you make it present, that is to say, one that is greater than the patient; and that you keep your hand on the patient’s side, and hold the shoulder down from the patient’s buttock, and keep the buttock high, so that the patient hangs down from the head.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	and another minister grasps the patient’s hand downwards towards the belly. And if the patient is too light, if you put anything with him, the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And thus we also remember in another way: if the head of the shoulder is long and round like a nail driven into the earth, and the bone is neither too thick nor too thin;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	then it must be gently grasped by the patient, but with a soft drape over it, and the patient must be kept long and still; and the limb must be extended from the other side, and the joint will return to its place without harm.</start_of_turn>
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	and if all these things do not make it return, if you do this cure: take a nail of about three fingers’ breadth, which has a head to enter into the socket, in this form:  </start_of_turn>
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lie upon the head of the shoulder, draped with a cloth, that it does not irritate the patient, and put from behind the patient’s back; extend your arms over the shoulder of the long kind, and support the limb on the shoulder, and the arm at the wrist, then put the arm over an inch of the scapula, and extend the hands forward, or leave the forearm hanging down from the other side: the shoulder joint is now restored.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is restored, in whatever way, if you put from behind the patient’s back a thumb of wool even, then put the dressing loosely of powder of wheat, with incense and alum of egg, upon the whole shoulder and around, then strain from behind the base of the thumb immediately, and turn the limb upon the dressing, and embrace the hand at its collar, and let the hands hang down alongside.</start_of_turn>
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he move little, until the limb is comfortable, because it will heal better; and then move more after five or six days, and turn; and if it is firm and is not softened, if it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	If the dislocation is urgent due to moisture, or for some other reason, if it is necessary to perform cautery, do so twice, if it is placed in front or alongside the cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	If you do all this, and the dislocation does not heal after twenty-three days, and the limb still cannot lift the upper arm, then know that the nerves at the head of the shoulder are compressed or stretched or softened; and that the dislocation will never heal in its place.</start_of_turn>
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is from front to back, and the bones, or behind, if it is done by impulse, and extension of the arms, and if another bandage is administered; and it is cured as long as it is healthy.</start_of_turn
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	If after healing the limb grieves and becomes stiff, if the patient uses it repeatedly, many times, until the grief is gone and returns to its first state.
de la dislocation dou coute	If after healing the limb grieves and becomes stiff, if the patient uses it repeatedly, many times, until the grief is gone and returns to its first state.
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	If after healing the limb grieves and becomes stiff, if the patient uses it repeatedly, many times, until the grief is gone and returns to its first state.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	If after healing the limb grieves and becomes stiff, if the patient uses it repeatedly, many times, until the grief is gone and returns to its first state
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must ensure that you reset it immediately, even if it comes loose again after you have set it; for if it comes loose again while it is healing, it will cause further pain. And by chance it will not be possible to restore it at all, even if it is at the back; in such a case it is better to leave it as it is rather than to cause further dislocation, which is more painful and can also lead to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And if it can be restored, when it is possible to restore it, extend your hand with both hands; spread your arms and hands as wide as the ruler allows, from armpit to wrist, front and back, and stabilize the joint with your thumbs together or at the root of the bone until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, if it returns when you double your hand over your hand, and grasp from the root of the bone that is loosened.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it does not return to its place, administer great extension; and if two ministers extend the arm and hold it by two ministers, if it does not move during extension; then turn the arm from the shoulder joint, and cover it with a double-layered drape that is long and wide.
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	When you see that the arm has been dislocated from its socket, if it has not been oiled with any oil to soften the joint, then immediately restore the dislocation, until it returns to its place
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	When it is in its place, put on dry bandages with eggshells, and strain the arm, and keep the arm bent towards the painful side, and leave it for a while, then remove it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly in its place, if you see that it does not hold firmly, repeat the manipulation of the limb and the support, and leave it thus for a few days, until it is firmly set; then you can remove the support.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	If after the joint has been repositioned, there is pain, and it moves, bathe and massage it well, and press until the pain is gone; or put a poultice of mutton fat on the joint, then leave it in place for a day and a night, and then remove the poultice and make the limb move again.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	When it sweats, wipe the joint gently, then put the poultice back on, and then move or bathe; and do this several times until it is healed; and if you see that it returns to its place, put on a wet cloth soaked in urine and bind it up; if it returns to its normal position.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand is loosened, and its return is laborious, more than other joints in general; it must be immediately repositioned to its place, even if it is loosened, or if there is bleeding or swelling
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And it must be that you place the painful hand on a table, and extend the limb, and look at it so that it is even, until it puts its palm on the surface of the joint, and holds it until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	However, you must look to see if it is well in place; then put the painful side of the hand on a table when extending and repositioning it
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele aparance de la jointure. S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	If the dislocation is at the back of the hand, place the patient's hand face down on the table, and hold their other hand on the appearance of the joint. If it returns to its place, it is well.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, if the strain of the muscles is relaxed after the incisions, let them remain in their natural position and slowly return to their starting point.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if it cannot endure it, and you do not put it back in place after a few days, the dislocation will persist.</start_of_turn
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	and do not harm the patient in any way until the hands are relaxed, and do not attempt to extract anything: for if the nerves are cut or the vessels; except in cases where it is necessary to extract by cautery, which is of little value.

de la dislocation des dois de la main	... until the dislocation of the shoulder of the hand.</start_of_turn>

des dislocations de la hainche	dislocations of the hip joint.
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	The joints of the hip and the shoulder only dislocate; it does not happen with other joints; and the hip joint is damaged in three parts: front and back, and top and bottom; the more it is damaged from front to back, and the more it is damaged from top to bottom.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And thus is known of a dislocation when, after uniting the affected limb with the sinew, the patient’s knee becomes longer and more painful than before; and he cannot double his knee over a fire.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And it is known that a dislocation is often caused by excessive swelling of the abscess, for the head of the humerus comes loose from its socket.</start_of_turn>

de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	And when they are even, and nothing is open, if you put on the plant of rue over a table at a quarter past nine, then the swelling forms, and you leave it for two days, and then you take it off; and you rest it until it is healed.
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	And when they are even, and nothing is open, if you put on the plant of rue over a table at a quarter past nine, then the swelling forms, and you leave it for two days, and then you take it off; and you rest it until it is healed.
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	If you are not humble in your cure, and if you are not skilled in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and timely, do not dare;
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	If you are not humble in your cure, and if you are not skilled in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and timely, do not dare; use calming measures at the outset and leave the patient in the hands of God, if you do not see hope of salvation.</start_of_turn>
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	And when you see hope, if you now reset the limb, even if the abscess remains;
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	When the limb is at rest, if necessary, administer calming things around the wound, and cure the wound if possible, with dried sponges.
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	When the dislocation breaks bones and soft tissue, if the bones are loose, do as in ordinary ailments;.</start_of_turn>
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors. Amen	Beware of entering into fear, as I have said, for this is harmful to you both physically and spiritually, as it brings God’s wrath upon you and endangers your body and soul. Amen.</start_of_turn>
Explicit le romen de fisique	Describe the physical symptom.</start_of_turn
